# Capabilities тАФ the loop's only success metric

Append-only inventory of **real, user-exercisable** Muse
capabilities. One line per capability: what the user can do, the
exact command/surface, and the executable check that proves it.

Rules (enforced by `.claude/rules/iteration-loop.md`):

- Every shipped outward goal MUST append exactly one new line here.
  The `<check>` MUST be a concrete automated test or smoke id that
  actually runs green under `pnpm check` / `pnpm smoke:broad` /
  `pnpm smoke:live` and asserts the *capability* end-to-end (not
  that code compiles). Prose with no runnable id is not a check.
- **Cross-time falsification:** every iteration's first action is
  to run the newest line's check and prove it still passes. A
  faked/broken line = the next iteration's whole job is to fix it.
- **Regression sweep:** every 10th iteration re-runs ALL checks;
  any regression = next iteration must restore it.
- A request/response-path capability whose `smoke:live` did NOT
  actually run is tagged `[UNVERIFIED-LIVE]`; it does not count
  until a later iteration runs the live check and drops the tag.
- Append-only. Never delete or weaken a line.
- **The success metric is NOT this line count.** It is
  `OUTWARD-TARGETS.md` bullets flipped `[ ]`тЖТ`[x]`. A line here is
  the *evidence* for a flip (cite the bullet it delivers); a line
  that adds no bullet flip is thin and does not satisfy the metric.
  No bullet flipped in the last 5 iterations тЗТ next iteration's
  sole mandate is to flip one end-to-end. Flat bullets =
  degeneration; act on it тАФ never stop, never ask a human.

Format: `- [<axis>] <capability> тАФ <command/surface> тАФ <runnable check id> тАФ P<n> bullet`
axis тИИ Reach | Anticipation | Autonomy | Presence

## Inventory

P0тАУP21's full verified ledger is preserved in
`archive/CAPABILITIES-through-2026-05-27.md` (human reset
2026-05-27 to keep the loop-facing file lean тАФ history intact, not
deleted). The lines below are the delivered foundation that the
active P22 target extends; new P22 lines append here.

- [Anticipation] Proactive notice loop (upcoming events / reminders) тАФ `apps/api` proactive daemon tick тАФ `apps/api` proactive-tick tests
- [Anticipation] Self-queued follow-up promises fire later тАФ followups daemon tick тАФ `runDueFollowups` tests
- [Autonomy] Standing-objective evaluation fires its actuator тАФ objectives daemon tick тАФ `runDueObjectives` tests
- [Anticipation] Ambient OS signal drives a proactive notice тАФ `runAmbientNoticeTick` + `MacOsActiveWindowSource` тАФ ambient-notice-loop tests
- [Anticipation] Page-change web-watch fires an edge-triggered notice тАФ `createWebWatchRunner` (HTTP + Chrome source) тАФ web-watch-runner / web-watch-chrome tests
- [Anticipation] Proactive notice delivered to a real channel тАФ `ProactiveNoticeSink` over the messaging registry (Telegram) тАФ `sendWithRetry` + proactive-notice-loop tests
- [Anticipation] One-process daemon launcher fires a real proactive tick тАФ `muse daemon --once` тАФ `apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.test.ts` (imminent task delivered to a contract-faithful messaging sink; quiet tick sends nothing; unknown provider fails closed) тАФ P22-1a bullet
- [Presence] Episode forgetting is now importance-aware тАФ a pivotal old session resists being vacuumed away while a trivial recent one fades (FadeMem, arXiv 2601.18642: biologically-inspired forgetting, decay modulated by importance) тАФ `vacuumEpisodes` dropped purely-oldest-by-`endedAt` at the cap; now `computeEpisodeRetention` scores each episode `exp(-ageDays / (halfLife┬╖(1 + w┬╖importance/10)))` so importance EXTENDS the half-life (importance-10 тЗТ ~3├Ч slower fade), and `selectRetainedEpisodes` keeps the highest-retention `cap` (newest-then-id tie-break). Back-compatible: an UNSCORED corpus reduces to recency ordering, so chronological vacuum is byte-identical until importance is present тАФ `@muse/mcp` episode-retention.test.ts (age decay; importance slows fade; unscoredтЖТrecency; unparseableтЖТ0; importance tips comparable ages: a 35-day importance-10 session out-retains a 25-day importance-1 one at the cap; deterministic ties) + existing vacuum suite stays green (unscored episodes still pruned oldest-first) тАФ research-applied slice (no new dep, deterministic/local; builds on the importance arc)
- [Presence] Auto-extracted memory now resolves each fact with an explicit operation instead of blind-overwriting (Mem0, arXiv 2504.19413: per-candidate ADD/UPDATE/DELETE/NOOP) тАФ `classifyMemoryOperation(existing, incoming)` is deterministic over the extractor's output (no extra model call): NOOP when a value re-confirms what's stored тЖТ SKIPS the redundant write + provenance entry (a re-mention no longer logs a fresh "learned" event); DELETE when the value is a no-value/retraction token (none/n/a/unknown/ьЧЖьЭМ/ыкиыжД/тАж) тЖТ the key is FORGOTTEN via the store's `forget` instead of storing junk like "unknown"; ADD/UPDATE upsert + record provenance as before; the auto-extract persist reads existing memory once and routes each fact/preference through it тАФ `@muse/memory` memory-operation.test.ts (classifier: add/noop/update/delete EN+KO tokens; auto-extract integration: re-confirm тЖТ no new provenance, changed тЖТ upsert+provenance, retraction тЖТ key forgotten) + full memory suite 213 green (new facts still ADD as before, back-compatible) тАФ research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; deterministic, no new dep, no extra LLM call)
- [Reach] A natural-language tool-selection path is available + measured against the native one (Natural Language Tools, arXiv 2510.14453: stating the tool choice in prose + parsing it deterministically beats forcing JSON on small/open-weight models) тАФ `parseNaturalLanguageToolSelection(text, toolNames)` deterministically maps a model's prose answer to one known tool (earliest-named wins; whole-token match so `time_now` тЙа `my_time_now_helper`; explicit no-tool/none/ьЧЖьЭМ тЖТ none) and `pnpm eval:tools:nl` compares NATIVE (Hermes JSON tool-call) vs NL one-shot accuracy on the confusable time set тАФ `@muse/tools` nl-tool-selection.test.ts (single pick, "use A not B"тЖТA, no-tool EN+KO, embedded-name not matched, empty) + LIVE qwen3:8b: native 7/7 (100%) AND NL 7/7 (100%) on the confusable time set тАФ verified finding: Muse's tuned tool names are ALREADY at the selection ceiling, so the NL path is kept as a reusable parser + comparison gate rather than wired (evidence-based: add NL complexity only when a confusable set's native accuracy drops below ceiling) тАФ research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; no new dep, core tool path untouched)
- [Presence] Muse applies LEARNED STRATEGIES from past feedback, not just avoidances тАФ a self-improving playbook (ACE тАФ Agentic Context Engineering, arXiv 2510.04618: a frozen model improves by accumulating small strategy deltas in an evolving context, no fine-tuning) тАФ the POSITIVE counterpart to veto-avoidance: `applyPlaybook` injects a `[Learned Strategies]` system block (mirrors the veto-avoidance seam; conservative тАФ zero strategies/no userId тЗТ exact no-op; fail-open) wired into the live agent-runtime context pipeline behind a duck-typed `PlaybookProvider`; the durable `~/.muse/playbook.json` store (`@muse/mcp`, atomic/tolerant/capped) is adapted by `buildPlaybookProvider` (MUSE_PLAYBOOK default-on) and populated via `muse playbook add|list|remove` тАФ `@muse/agent-core` playbook.test.ts (conservative/fail-open/inject + injection-collapse + LIVE-runtime wiring: a recorded strategy reaches a real createAgentRuntime run's system prompt, none тЖТ no-op) + LIVE qwen3:8b EFFECT MEASUREMENT: with the strategy "answer in at most 6 words" injected, a question that drew a long multi-paragraph reply WITHOUT it returned a 7-word "Paris. Famous for art, fashion, and culture." WITH it тАФ the learned strategy measurably changed the model's output тАФ research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; no new dep; mirrors the proven veto-avoidance pattern end-to-end)

- [Presence] The learned-strategy playbook injects only the strategies RELEVANT to the current turn, not the whole bank (ReasoningBank, arXiv 2509.25140: a self-evolving agent retrieves relevant reasoning memory rather than dumping it) тАФ `rankPlaybookStrategies` (CJK-aware token-overlap + tag boost, top-K with a recency floor so a non-empty bank never injects zero) wired into BOTH `applyPlaybook` (runtime `--with-tools`) and the chat-only `muse ask` path via `selectPlaybookSection` (env `MUSE_PLAYBOOK_INJECT_TOPK`, default 6); when the bank is тЙд topK the SET is unchanged (today's inject-all), only ordered most-relevant-first тАФ `packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts` (relevance ranks above irrelevant; тЙдK returns all best-first; >K drops least-relevant; recency floor on zero-overlap; Korean CJK match; applyPlaybook orders by the latest user message) + `apps/cli/src/commands-ask-playbook.test.ts` (an email prompt injects the email strategy and drops a scheduling-only one at topK=1) тАФ research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; deterministic, no new dep, no extra LLM call; foundation for slice-2 correction-driven auto-distillation)
- [Presence] Muse auto-LEARNS a strategy from a correction the user made тАФ at session end it distills a generalised `[Learned Strategies]` entry from a corrected exchange into the SAME `~/.muse/playbook.json` (ReasoningBank, arXiv 2509.25140: a self-evolving agent distills reusable strategies from its own experience; the outcome signal is the RELIABLE explicit correction, NOT small-model self-judgement per arXiv 2404.17140) тАФ auto at REPL exit (`MUSE_PLAYBOOK_DISTILL_ENABLED`, default off) + manual `muse playbook distill`; pipeline = `detectCorrections` (EN+KO, precision-first rule pass) тЖТ `distillStrategyFromCorrection` (one LLM call, secret-redacted, fail-soft) тЖТ `strategyTextSimilarity` dedup (тЙе0.6, makes re-runs idempotent) тЖТ `recordPlaybookStrategy` тАФ `packages/agent-core/test/correction-distiller.test.ts` (detector EN+KO + false-positive guard + no-prior-assistant + cap; distiller parse/omit-tag/fail-soft) + `playbook.test.ts` (similarity) + `apps/cli/src/chat-distill-corrections.test.ts` (records from a corrected session, skips no-correction, dedups, skips no-userId) + `commands-playbook.test.ts` (distill subcommand); LIVE qwen3:8b: the Korean correction "ъ╖╕ъ▓М ьХДыЛИыЭ╝ ы╢Иыж┐ эПмьЭ╕эК╕ыбЬ ьаХыжмэХ┤ьдШ" distilled "when asked to summarise, use bullet points not prose" into the playbook end-to-end via `muse playbook distill` тАФ research-applied slice (arXiv ids cited in code; deterministic detection+dedup, single offline LLM call, no new dep; completes ReasoningBank retrievalтЖТdistillation)
- [Knowledge] knowledge_search grades retrieval confidence and FRAMES weak grounding as low-confidence instead of telling the small local model to cite it (CRAG, arXiv 2401.15884: a lightweight retrieval evaluator scores evidence quality) тАФ `classifyRetrievalConfidence` over the TOP match's ABSOLUTE cosine (surfaced as `KnowledgeMatch.cosine`, separate from the hybrid RRF `score`): confidentтЖТ"cite the [source]", ambiguousтЖТ"Possibly-related (LOW confidence тАФ verify, don't cite as fact)", noneтЖТno passages; `renderKnowledgeMatches` (the agent `knowledge_search` + notes corpus-search tools) and the ambient `createKnowledgeEnricher` (Related line only when confident) gate on it тАФ `packages/agent-core/test/knowledge-recall-agent.test.ts` (verdict none/ambiguous/confident; cosine surfaced in both paths; render header by verdict) + `knowledge-render-litm.test.ts` + `packages/autoconfigure/test/knowledge-enricher*.test.ts` (weak match тЖТ no Related line) тАФ research-applied slice. HONEST scope: live-calibrated on nomic-embed (relevant ~0.61 vs personal distractors ~0.44тАУ0.51 тЖТ `confidentAt` 0.55), but nomic's cosine space is compressed (unrelated encyclopedic text can score ~0.54), so this is a BEST-EFFORT low-confidence flag for personal corpora, not a hard relevant/irrelevant separator (same honesty class as the P24-2 MMR nudge). No web fallback (deferred); deterministic, no new dep, no extra round
- [Autonomy] The plan-execute planner reuses a similar PAST plan as a few-shot exemplar so the small local model plans better in one shot (Agentic Plan Caching, arXiv 2506.14852: extract plan templates from completed runs and reuse them on similar tasks) тАФ completed plans auto-captured to `~/.muse/plan-cache.json`, retrieved by Jaccard token overlap (`selectPlanExemplar`, reuses `strategyTextSimilarity`), rendered as a `[Similar Past Plan]` block injected into the planning prompt before `[User Request]`; threaded `PlanCacheProvider` тЖТ `PlanExecuteRunner` тЖТ `AgentRuntime`, built by `buildPlanCacheProvider` (default-on, opt out `MUSE_PLAN_CACHE=false`), conservative (no userId / no match тЗТ no exemplar + no record), fail-open тАФ `packages/agent-core/test/plan-cache.test.ts` (retrieval picks most-similar / none below threshold; render shape) + `agent-runtime-plan-cache.test.ts` (a plan-execute run records its plan; a cached similar plan is injected into the planning request; no userId тЗТ neither) + `packages/mcp/test/personal-plan-cache-store.test.ts` (record/query/filter/upsert/cap/tolerant) + `packages/prompts/test/prompts.test.ts` (exemplar before [User Request]) тАФ research-applied slice. HONEST scope: this is APC's faithful store/match adapted for a LOCAL free model as planning GUIDANCE (improves one-shot plan reliability), NOT APC's skip-the-planner efficiency play (cloud cost benefit is moot locally; exact repeats already covered by responseCache). Deterministic, no new dep, no extra model round
- [Autonomy] Muse AUTHORS a reusable SKILL.md from a procedural user correction at session end (fork-and-review, after Hermes Agent's background-review loop, MIT тАФ see THIRD_PARTY_NOTICES.md) тАФ deterministic `detectSkillCandidates` (reuses `detectCorrections`, EN+KO) тЖТ one local-Qwen `draftSkillFromSignal` (returns `NONE` for mere preferences so those stay playbook-only, secret-redacted, fail-soft) тЖТ `AuthoredSkillStore.writeOrPatch` (EXECUTE-GATED by type: a SkillDraft has no `requires` field so an authored skill can never declare runnable bins тЖТ `muse.skills.run` refuses it until a human promotes it; dedupтЖТpatch/skip, cap 30 with archive-never-delete, atomic fsync+rename 0600) into `~/.muse/skills/authored/`, loaded as the LOWEST-precedence registry root (a same-named user/workspace skill always wins) so it is picked up next session and surfaced by `selectRelevantSkills` on a similar request; auto at REPL exit (`MUSE_SKILL_AUTHOR_ENABLED`, default off) + manual `muse skills author` тАФ `packages/skills/test/authored-skill-store.test.ts` (create + execute-gate + dedup patch/skip + cap-archive + collision suffix) + `packages/agent-core/test/skill-review.test.ts` (detect EN+KO + cap; draft parse / NONEтЖТnull / malformedтЖТnull / fail-soft) + `packages/autoconfigure/test/skills-registry-precedence.test.ts` (user overrides authored; authored-only still loads) + `apps/cli/src/chat-author-skills.test.ts` (authors from a corrected session, skips no-correction, fail-soft, AND end-to-end: authored тЖТ loaded next session via buildSkillRegistry тЖТ selected by selectRelevantSkills on a similar request, not on an unrelated one); `pnpm check` + `pnpm lint` 0/0 + `pnpm smoke:live` (request path unaffected) тАФ self-improvement slice (the inputs already existed тАФ ReasoningBank distiller, reflection, UserModel; this is the missing bridge: experience тЖТ durable reusable skill)

- [Knowledge] Muse synthesises GROUNDED reflections ("dreaming") тАФ higher-level insights about the user from recent episodes/notes тАФ that CANNOT make things up (after OpenClaw's dreaming + Generative Agents reflection, arXiv 2304.03442; honest/local Muse key) тАФ `synthesizeReflections` (agent-core) prompts the LOCAL model over `{id,text}` items; `parseReflections` deterministically strips any cited source id absent from the inputs and drops a reflection below `minSupport` distinct real sources, so an insight can only be grounded in episodes the user actually has тАФ `packages/agent-core/src/reflection-synthesis.test.ts` (11: grounding strips invented ids, minSupport, dedupe, junk-tolerant JSON, fail-soft) + a LIVE qwen3:8b battery `apps/cli/scripts/verify-reflection-synthesis.mjs` in `eval:self-improving` (a recurring networking theme across 3 episodes synthesised + grounded in the right real ids; grounding invariant holds for every reflection); `pnpm lint` 0/0 тАФ P32-1 differentiation slice (idle-daemon wiring + persistence is P32-2)
- [Knowledge] `muse reflections [refresh]` surfaces Muse's GROUNDED "dreaming" тАФ higher-level insights about the user synthesised from past episodes, each citing the real episodes it came from (P32-2; OpenClaw dreaming + Generative Agents reflection in Muse's honest/local key) тАФ `reflections-store` (atomic + mutation-queued, dedup on normalised insight, FIFO-trim) + `muse reflections refresh` (reads recent episodes тЖТ `synthesizeReflections` over the local model тЖТ `addReflections`, dedup) + `muse reflections` (lists newest-first WITH source episode ids). - [Reach] Muse-to-Muse SWARM shares KNOW-HOW only (skills/strategies/reasoning), NEVER personal data, with inbound INERT тАФ `muse swarm share|serve|pending|promote`: a peer's shared skill crosses as a PII-redacted, HMAC-signed A2A `message/send`, lands QUARANTINED on the receiver (a peer can never trigger compute), and runs nothing until the user promotes it to an EXECUTE-GATED authored skill (no `requires:` тЖТ `muse.skills.run` refuses it). - [Autonomy] Muse runs REINFORCEMENT LEARNING over its learned-strategy playbook (model is fixed тЖТ RL on the MEMORY, not the weights): each strategy carries a clamped `reward` that reward-weighted `rankPlaybookStrategies` blends into selection, so a proven strategy surfaces first and one that keeps getting corrected DECAYS out of the injected top-K; the signal is AUTOMATIC тАФ at session end the strategy a correction implicates (most similar to the corrected request) is docked via `adjustPlaybookReward`, alongside ReasoningBank distillation of the new lesson. Reward flows through BOTH injection paths (agent-runtime `buildPlaybookProvider` + chat-only `muse ask` `selectPlaybookSection`); `muse playbook` shows each strategy's learned reward and `muse playbook distill` reports what it decayed тАФ `packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts` (reward breaks a relevance tie; a тИТ5 strategy sinks out of top-K below a fresh peer; absent reward == 0; `clampReward` bounds) + `packages/mcp/test/playbook-store.test.ts` (`adjustPlaybookReward` accumulates/clamps/unknown-id/non-finite no-op; back-compat read of a reward-less entry; non-numeric reward quarantined) + `apps/cli/src/chat-distill-corrections.test.ts` (a corrected session docks the implicated strategy to тИТ1, unrelated untouched). LIVE: `muse playbook list` renders тЯиreward +3тЯй/тЯиreward тИТ4тЯй and a тИТ4 prose strategy is deranked below an equally-relevant bullet strategy through the BUILT CLI; `pnpm check` green (agent-core 1064 / mcp 1108 / autoconfigure 450 / cli 1547 / api 747) + `pnpm lint` 0/0 тАФ P33-1 RL slice (ACE arXiv 2510.04618 + the sibling veto store; reward-shaped, model-fixed)
- [Autonomy] The RL reward signal is now BIDIRECTIONAL тАФ an explicit user APPROVAL reinforces the strategy that applied, the mirror of correction-driven decay, so the playbook learns from both "you got it right" and "you got it wrong" (not just absence-of-negative). `detectApprovals` (agent-core) is a precision-first EN+KO detector mirroring `detectCorrections` (fires on "perfect"/"exactly right"/"nailed it"/"ьЩДы▓╜эХ┤"/"ыФ▒ ьвЛьХД"/"ы░ФыбЬ ъ╖╕ъ▒░ьХ╝" тАФ NOT bare "ok"/"thanks"/"ьвЛьХД"/"ъ│аызИьЫМ", which acknowledge but don't endorse); at session end `distillSessionCorrections` credit-assigns each approval to the existing strategy most similar to its request and REINFORCES it (+1, `adjustPlaybookReward`), once per strategy (never both decayed and reinforced in one session), alongside correction-decay + distillation. `muse playbook distill` now reports both тЖС reinforced and тЖУ decayed тАФ `packages/agent-core/test/correction-distiller.test.ts` (detectApprovals: 13 EN+KO endorsements fire, 9 bare-acknowledgement phrases do NOT, assistantтЖТuser pairing + request backfill + maxExchanges cap) + `apps/cli/src/chat-distill-corrections.test.ts` (an approval session with no correction lifts the applied strategy to +1, unrelated untouched, status still "skipped"-for-distillation). agent-core 1068 / cli 1548 tests pass + `pnpm lint` 0/0 тАФ P33-2 RL slice (bidirectional reward from explicit feedback)
- [Autonomy] LEARNED AVOIDANCE closes the RL extinction loop тАФ a strategy corrected into the floor (reward тЙд `PLAYBOOK_AVOID_BELOW` = тИТ4, ~4 implicating corrections) is EXCLUDED from injection ENTIRELY, not merely deranked: `rankPlaybookStrategies` filters it out before selection even when the bank is тЙд topK (where ranking otherwise returns everything, so a deeply-negative strategy would still slip into a small bank). Soft + reversible (the veto-store parallel): it stays in the bank, shows in `muse playbook` as "┬╖ avoided (not injected)", and a later approval can lift its reward back above the line. `isAvoidedStrategy` is the shared predicate тАФ `packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts` (an avoided strategy is dropped even at bank тЙд topK; reward тИТ3 still injects ranked last; all-avoided тЖТ empty; `isAvoidedStrategy` boundary incl. absent=not-avoided). - [Autonomy] The RL reward loop now spans AUTHORED SKILLS too, not just the strategy playbook тАФ a skill the user keeps correcting stops being applied; one they approve earns standing (the same decay/reinforce/avoid mechanics, extended to a second memory type). A sidecar `skill-rewards.json` (nameтЖТreward, kept OUT of each SKILL.md so a decay never rewrites the body) holds the reward; `adjustSkillReward` (clamped, mutation-queued) moves it; at session end `applySkillRewardsFromSession` credit-assigns each correction/approval to the authored skill the live prompt WOULD have applied тАФ via the SAME `selectRelevantSkills` the per-turn prompt uses, so credit lands on the skill that actually applied тАФ and decays (тИТ1) / reinforces (+1) it; `buildSkillsPrompt` then DROPS an avoided skill (reward тЙд `SKILL_AVOID_BELOW` = тИТ4) from the per-turn prompt entirely (no body, not even an index line). `muse skills authored` shows each skill's reward + "┬╖ avoided (not applied)" тАФ `packages/mcp/test/skill-rewards-store.test.ts` (read/clamp/adjust/avoid-boundary) + `apps/cli/src/chat-skills.test.ts` (selectRelevantSkills + buildSkillsPrompt drop an avoided skill, keep the rest) + `apps/cli/src/chat-author-skills.test.ts` (a corrected request decays the applied skill to тИТ1, an approval reinforces to +1, a bare ack тЖТ no change). - [Autonomy] The user can STEER the RL reward directly тАФ `muse playbook reward <id> [amount] [--down]` and `muse skills reward <name> [amount] [--down]` manually reinforce (or, with `--down`, penalise) a learned strategy/skill, clamped via the SAME `adjustPlaybookReward`/`adjustSkillReward` the auto-signal uses. So a strategy/skill the auto-loop wrongly penalised can be RESCUED back above the avoid line, and a known-good one PRE-TRUSTED тАФ the reversibility + control that makes the (default-off) auto-RL safe to turn on. `amount` is a positive integer (default 1) so `--down` sidesteps commander parsing a leading `-` as a flag; an unknown id/name is refused and never written тАФ `apps/cli/src/commands-playbook.test.ts` (reinforces +amount, --down penalises, clamps, prefix-matched id, unknown id refused) + `apps/cli/src/commands-skills.test.ts` (adjusts an authored skill, --down penalises, unknown skill refused + not written; `resolveSkillRewardsFile` env/default). - [Knowledge/Edge] `muse ask` no longer FALSE-REFUSES a question its corpus answers when the answer note's embedding cosine ranks below near-misses тАФ the headline chat-only recall path is now HYBRID (embedding-cosine + lexical keyword RRF), the same fusion the `knowledge_search` agent path already used (P23, RRF: Cormack et al. SIGIR 2009), but it was never applied to the headline `muse ask` path, which ranked notes by PURE cosine. On nomic's compressed embedding space a query with strong distinctive terms ("WireGuard", "MTU") ranked the one answer-bearing note ~5th, so the default top-3 excluded it and Muse honestly-but-WRONGLY said "I'm not sure" тАФ the "GUARD THE EDGE" failure mode (a false refusal turns honest into useless). `diversifyAskChunks` gains an optional `query`: when present it fuses the cosine rank with a lexical-overlap rank (reusing agent-core's now-exported `lexicalTokens`/`lexicalOverlap`/`fuseByReciprocalRank`) via RRF, normalises the fused relevance to [0,1] so MMR's diversity term stays comparable, and selects the top-K from that тАФ WITHOUT re-embedding (index embeddings reused) and KEEPING each chunk's absolute cosine `score` so the CRAG confidence framing is unchanged; a stopword-only query falls back to the prior cosine MMR тАФ `apps/cli/src/commands-ask-mmr.test.ts` (hybrid: a keyword-matching answer note that pure-cosine top-3 EXCLUDES is rescued into the top-3; the rescued chunk keeps its absolute cosine 0.50; a stopword-only query is byte-identical to cosine selection). - [Self-learning] Learned strategies now FADE when you stop reinforcing them (B1 Slice 2, continuous RL disuse-decay) тАФ a one-off thumbs-up no longer steers Muse forever. - [Self-learning] A reinforced strategy is no longer forgotten just for being old (B1 Slice 3 тАФ reward-/recency-weighted eviction). When the learned-strategy playbook overflows its 100-entry cap, eviction was blind FIFO (drop the oldest regardless of value), so a strategy you reinforced repeatedly could be evicted while a never-used newer one survived. New `retainPlaybookEntries` (mcp) keeps the highest-value entries instead тАФ value = reward, then recency: a high-reward OLD strategy beats a low-reward NEW one, reward ties break toward the newer, negative/avoided entries are evicted first, and survivors keep their original insertion order (the recency proxy `rankPlaybookStrategies` relies on). `recordPlaybookStrategy` now caps via this helper instead of `.slice(-MAX)`. Proof: unit tests in `packages/mcp/test/playbook-store.test.ts` (at/under cap returned unchanged; high-reward-old kept over low-reward-new with order preserved; reward-tieтЖТrecency; avoided evicted before neutral/positive; record-path overflow of 120 neutral fillers keeps a +5 champion) + a LIVE end-to-end run on this box (HOME-isolated mock playbook, never real ~/.muse): a `+5` champion recorded FIRST then buried under 120 newer neutral records survived the cap and `muse playbook list` shows `[champion] тЯиreward +5тЯй` still present, total capped at 100 (blind FIFO would have dropped it as oldest). mcp 1227 tests + `pnpm lint` 0/0 тАФ the bank now keeps what you've proven matters, not merely what's newest тАФ P36-12 bullet
- [Self-learning] `muse learned` now shows the WHY behind each learned strategy (B1 Slice 4 тАФ provenance + legibility). A strategy used to be just a sentence; now each carries its ORIGIN (`grounded` = distilled from a real correction, `reflected` = synthetic, `manual` = you typed it) and the `source` correction that taught it, so `muse learned` prints "тЖ│ learned from your correction: '<the exact thing you said>'" under both trusted and probation strategies тАФ the legibility precondition to trusting unattended learning (you can judge whether to keep what Muse learned). PlaybookEntry/PlaybookStrategy gain `origin`/`source`; both correction-distill writers (idle daemon `distill-queue.ts` + chat-exit `chat-distill-corrections.ts`) stamp `origin: "grounded"` + the correction; `renderLearnedDigest` renders the why line; and a small ranking tie-break (`REFLECTED_RANK_PENALTY`, far below a reward step or relevance point) makes a `reflected` strategy never outrank an otherwise-equal `grounded` one тАФ evidence beats synthesis at a dead heat. Proof: unit tests in `packages/mcp/test/playbook-store.test.ts` (origin/source round-trip + non-string-drops), `packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts` (grounded outranks equal reflected; penalty is tie-break-only, a more-relevant reflected still wins), `apps/cli/src/commands-learned.test.ts` (why line for grounded incl. probation; reflected flagged synthetic; long source truncated; legacy/manual gets no line) + a LIVE full chain on qwen3:8b (HOME-isolated, never real ~/.muse): enqueue "no, that is not what I meant тАФ give me bullet points, not prose" тЖТ idle `distillQueuedCorrections` тЖТ `muse learned` printed the probation strategy WITH "тЖ│ learned from your correction: '<that correction>'". agent-core 1238 / mcp 1229 / api 817 / cli 1618 tests + `pnpm lint` 0/0 тАФ the user can now SEE why Muse believes each learned thing тАФ P36-13 bullet
- [Self-learning] `muse playbook undo <id>` now makes Muse forget a learned strategy AND not re-learn it (B1 Slice 5 тАФ undo that TEACHES; `--pause` deferred). Plain `remove` only deletes a strategy, so the idle distiller re-learns the same lesson the next time the user gives a similar correction. `undo` removes the strategy AND records a suppressed-lesson veto keyed on its SOURCE correction (the provenance captured by P36-13), so the idle daemon distiller skips that signal BEFORE the LLM call and bumps the veto's blocked counter. Keying on the stable correction signal (not the LLM's run-to-run paraphrase of the strategy) is what makes the suppression actually stick тАФ a flaw the live test caught and drove the redesign. New `suppressed-lessons.json` store (`packages/mcp/src/suppressed-lessons-store.ts`: record/read/query/incrementBlocked, atomic, capped) + `resolveSuppressedLessonsFile` (autoconfigure); `distill-queue.ts` (api) consults it via `strategyTextSimilarity` on the source; `muse playbook undo` (cli) wires it. Proof: unit tests in `packages/mcp/test/suppressed-lessons-store.test.ts` (source round-trip, cap, blocked-counter), `apps/api/src/distill-queue.test.ts` (skips a matching correction before distilling + bumps counter; a different correction still distills; no-source can't block; back-compat without the file), `apps/cli/src/commands-playbook.test.ts` (undo removes + records the veto with source) + a LIVE full chain on qwen3:8b (HOME-isolated, never real ~/.muse): correction тЖТ idle distill тЖТ `muse playbook undo` тЖТ the SAME correction re-enqueued distilled 0 (veto blockedCount 1) while a DIFFERENT correction still learned. mcp 1234 / api 823 / cli 1619 tests + `pnpm lint` 0/0 тАФ the user is now in control of what Muse keeps learning тАФ P36-14 bullet
- [Self-learning] `muse playbook pause` now stops ALL background self-learning with one command (B1 Slice 5 complete тАФ the kill-switch half). - [Edge/Grounding] `muse ask` now catches the WRONG-VALUE answer the lexical rubric was blind to (P38-2). - [Edge/Constructive] `muse ask --repair` makes the edge CONSTRUCTIVE тАФ an ungrounded answer is corrected, not just warned (P38-3). When the recall wedge returns ungrounded, `--repair` runs ONE local pass that rewrites the answer constrained to the retrieved evidence and shows it as "ЁЯФз Corrected from your notes" ONLY if the rewrite re-verifies GROUNDED through the SAME gate (citation check + rubric + the P38-2 claim-level value escalation тАФ so a wrong value can't survive into the fix). Fail-CLOSED: a refusing / gate-failing / still-ungrounded / no-evidence rewrite leaves the honest refusal standing тАФ a fix is never fabricated. Opt-in (one extra inference). - [Edge/Recall] `muse ask` now refuses a question whose only retrieval is a flat off-corpus near-miss, instead of presenting it as confident (P38-4, adaptive confidence calibration). Near nomic's compressed-cosine floor a single absolute bar is fragile тАФ an out-of-corpus query ("how much did I spend on groceries last month?") clipped a near-miss note at 0.563 > the 0.55 bar, so `classifyRetrievalConfidence` said `confident` and the model was invited to cite it. The gate now demotes a `confident` top that is BOTH borderline (within 0.05 of the floor) AND flat (topтИТrunner-up < 0.08 тАФ the query matches several notes weakly, not one strongly) to `ambiguous`, while a clearly-high top or a clear lead stays confident so genuine single-note matches are untouched. Calibrated from the live per-case margins (the lowest confident answerable sits at 0.627 with a 0.18 gap, far outside the band; only the flat near-miss flips). Drives both the recall framing and the proactivity gate. - [Actuation] `muse ask "remind me this weekend / by end of the month тАж" --with-tools` now works тАФ more everyday date phrases land (P40-2). - [Front-door/Privacy] `muse doctor` now reports the TRUE local-only model instead of a misleading "inferred from GEMINI_API_KEY" (P34-12). Under MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY (default-ON, the core privacy posture), the model router IGNORES any ambient cloud key and runs the local ollama/qwen3:8b (per resolveDefaultModel) тАФ but the doctor's model-env check did NOT account for local-only: on any box that merely carried a GEMINI_API_KEY in the environment, it printed "[warn] model env: inferred from GEMINI_API_KEY". So a privacy-bound user running `muse doctor` precisely to CONFIRM that nothing leaves their machine was told their model is Gemini тАФ the diagnostic undercut the exact guarantee local-only exists to provide. Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-doctor.ts by extracting a pure, exported `modelEnvCheck(env)` that mirrors the runtime's resolveDefaultModel exactly: an explicit MUSE_MODEL is reported verbatim; under local-only (parseBoolean(MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY, true)) it reports "ollama/qwen3:8b (local-only default тАФ ambient cloud keys ignored)" as OK; and the cloud-credential inference WARN ("inferred from GEMINI_API_KEY (MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY=false)") appears ONLY under an explicit opt-out. Bonus fix: the doctor's downstream "ollama model pulled" check now uses the RESOLVED model (resolveDefaultModel(env)) instead of the raw MUSE_MODEL env, so under local-only тАФ where no MUSE_MODEL is set тАФ it now actually verifies qwen3:8b is pulled (5.2 GB), a check that was silently skipped before. Also exported LOCAL_FIRST_DEFAULT_MODEL from @muse/autoconfigure's index for the mirror. Proof: 5 new modelEnvCheck unit tests in apps/cli/src/commands-doctor.test.ts (local-only + GEMINI key тЖТ reports the local model NOT "inferred from GEMINI"; default env unset тЖТ local model; explicit MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY=false + key тЖТ warn inferred; explicit MUSE_MODEL reported verbatim; opt-out + no model + no key тЖТ fail) + 2 existing program.test.ts doctor tests corrected to set MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY=false where they intentionally exercise the cloud-inference fail/warn path + a LIVE `muse doctor` in all three scenarios (local-only+GEMINI тЖТ "тЬУ model env: ollama/qwen3:8b (local-only default тАФ ambient cloud keys ignored)" + "тЬУ ollama model: qwen3:8b pulled (5.2 GB)"; opt-out+GEMINI тЖТ warn inferred; explicit MUSE_MODEL тЖТ verbatim). cli 164 files / 1738 tests + autoconfigure 484 + pnpm lint 0/0 тАФ a privacy-conscious user can now trust `muse doctor` to truthfully confirm their model is local тАФ P34-12 bullet

- [Grounding edge/Perception] A Korean task / reminder / event recall now keeps its citation instead of being false-stripped тАФ the lexical citation gate tokenizes Unicode, and a coverage-only miss is routed to the judge, not hard-failed (P38-18). Probing ьзДьХИ's real Korean actuationтЖТrecall loop: `muse remind add "ыВ┤ьЭ╝ ьШдэЫД 3ьЛЬ" "ь╣Шъ│╝ ьШИьХ╜ ъ░Аъ╕░"` + `muse tasks add "ы╢Дъ╕░ ы│┤ъ│аьДЬ ьЮСьД▒эХШъ╕░"` both stored fine, but `muse ask "ыВ┤ъ░А эХ┤ьХ╝ эХа ьЭ╝ьЭ┤ ынРъ░А ьЮИьЦ┤?"` answered correctly and cited `[task: ы╢Дъ╕░ ы│┤ъ│аьДЬ ьЮСьД▒эХШъ╕░]` / `[reminder: ь╣Шъ│╝ ьШИьХ╜ ъ░Аъ╕░]` (the EXACT Korean titles) тАФ yet the citation gate STRIPPED both ("Removed 2 citations") and the rubric verdict false-flagged the answer. Root cause: `lexicalTokens` тАФ the token-overlap basis that `resolvesByOverlap` uses to validate the non-note citation classes (tasks / reminders / events / sessions / contacts / commands / commits / memories / actions) тАФ split on `/[^a-z0-9]+/` (ASCII only), so "ы╢Дъ╕░ ы│┤ъ│аьДЬ ьЮСьД▒эХШъ╕░" tokenized to `[]` (empty) тЖТ zero overlap with the Korean title тЖТ a perfectly valid Korean citation looked unresolvable and was dropped. Two coordinated fixes in packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts: (1) `lexicalTokens` now splits on Unicode `/[^\p{L}\p{N}]+/u` and KEEPS single-character CJK tokens (a 1-char Hanja/Hangul/Kana carries meaning) while still dropping 1-char Latin тАФ ASCII English tokenization is byte-for-byte unchanged (so no English regression); (2) because Unicode coverage of a CORRECT cross-lingual answer (Korean prose over English evidence) can legitimately dip below the coverage floor, `verifyGroundingWithReverify` now ESCALATES a confident, validly-cited coverage-only failure to the re-verification judge instead of hard-failing it тАФ the judge stays in the loop, so a WRONG cross-lingual value is still rejected, and a judge error fail-closes to ungrounded. Proof: 6 new agent-core unit tests (lexicalTokens tokenizes "ы╢Дъ╕░ ы│┤ъ│аьДЬ ьЮСьД▒эХШъ╕░" тЖТ {ы╢Дъ╕░, ы│┤ъ│аьДЬ, ьЮСьД▒эХШъ╕░}, keeps single-char CJK "ь░и"/"ы▓ИэШ╕эМР" but drops 1-char Latin x/y; the coverage-escalation upholds a correct cross-lingual answer to GROUNDED, keeps a wrong value UNGROUNDED when the judge rejects, fail-closes on a judge error, and does NOT escalate a coverage miss whose citation is INVALID) + the verify-claim-grounding battery still 6/6 on two consecutive runs (the cross-lingual correct/wrong cases route through the new branch) + LIVE on qwen3:8b: the Korean task/reminder recall above is now clean (no "Removed citation", no "treat as unverified"); the cross-lingual WiFi recall (P38-16) is unregressed; and a Korean absent-fact "ыВ┤ ьЧмъ╢М ы▓ИэШ╕ ынРьХ╝?" still refuses ("ьаХы│┤ьЧРыКФ ьЧмъ╢М ы▓ИэШ╕ьЧР ыМАэХЬ ыВ┤ьЪйьЭ┤ ьЧЖьК╡ыЛИыЛд") with no fabrication. agent-core 112 files / 1383 tests + cli 165 files / 1755 tests + cited-recall 6/6 + pnpm lint 0/0 тАФ a Korean-speaking user (or anyone whose tasks, reminders, and events are titled in their own language) now sees those recalls cited and un-warned instead of false-stripped as fabrications тАФ P38-18 bullet
- [Grounding edge] The grounding DRIFT verdict now runs under `muse ask --with-tools` too тАФ the agent (tool-using) recall path gets the same "treat as unverified" protection as chat-only, closing the one surface where "shows its work" was silent (P38-19). The recall edge's post-hoc rubric verdict (`groundingVerdictNotice` + the weak-band MaTTS reverify judge + the `--repair` offer) was gated `!options.withTools`, so a `muse ask --with-tools` answer that DRIFTED (asserted a value present in no source) printed confidently with NO grounding signal тАФ fabrication=0's "one deterministic grounding gate under EVERY surface" promise was literally false for the agent recall path. It had been skipped for a real reason: the verdict scores the answer against the CLI's pre-retrieval top-K notes (`scored`), but the `--with-tools` agent can pull a chunk via `knowledge_search` (often on a REFORMULATED query) that the top-K didn't include тАФ so scoring against `scored` alone would false-flag a legitimately grounded agent answer "treat as unverified". Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts: the verdict guard drops from `!options.json && !options.withTools` to `!options.json` (so it runs on both paths), and a new pure, exported `augmentNoteEvidenceWithCited(baseNotes, citedSources, liveNotes)` augments the verdict's note evidence with the FULL text of every note the answer ACTUALLY cites (each already gate-validated against the live corpus by the citation gate above) тАФ so a note the agent retrieved outside the top-K is always covered. The augmentation is ADDITIVE ONLY: it can only prevent a false "ungrounded", never cause a false "grounded" тАФ a drifted value that appears in no cited note still scores uncovered тЖТ ungrounded. Proof: 6 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/commands-ask-verdict-withtools.test.ts (pulls in a cited note's full chunks when the top-K missed it; ignores a note the answer never cited; never duplicates a chunk already in the base set; is a no-op when nothing or an invalid/stale source is cited; the additive-only invariant тАФ base evidence is never dropped or rewritten) + the existing verdict-source / grounding-verdict tests green + LIVE on qwen3:8b: a `muse ask --with-tools` answer asserting "WireGuard default MTU is 1420 [from net.md]" against a note that never states an MTU now fires "тЪая╕П Grounding check: this answer's claims aren't fully backed by your notes (low coverage rejected by re-verification) тАФ treat as unverified" + the `--repair` nudge (it was SILENT before this change); two grounded `--with-tools` answers (garage door code 4417, home wifi password) do NOT false-flag; and the chat-only path is byte-for-byte unchanged (only the `options.withTools && index` branch is new). cli 166 files / 1761 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 тАФ a user who runs `muse ask --with-tools` for a recall question now gets the same honest drift warning (and constructive --repair) as the plain ask, so the agent path can no longer present a fabricated value as a confident sourced fact тАФ P38-19 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Perception] `muse ask` no longer auto-saves the model's own answer as a durable "fact you told me" тАФ closing a provenance fabrication on the memory surface (P38-20). DISCOVERED live in P38-19's iteration and confirmed here: a `muse ask --with-tools` general-knowledge answer ("WireGuard default MTU is 1420") was silently persisted to `~/.muse/user-memory.json` as `wireguard_default_mtu: "1420"`, and the NEXT recall cited it `[memory: wireguard_default_mtu]` with the receipt "ЁЯза from what you told me" тАФ i.e. Muse asserting the USER had stated a fact the MODEL fabricated from general knowledge. Root cause: the shared user-memory auto-extract HOOK (`createUserMemoryAutoExtractHook.afterComplete`) mines the ASSISTANT output (not just the user's statements), and it was installed globally so it ran on EVERY agent run including one-shot `muse ask` recall тАФ so a question-answer turn distilled the model's own assertion as a user fact (a second, latent vector also existed: the `remember_fact` write tool was exposed on the recall agent). Fixed by making recall read-only for durable memory: in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts the `--with-tools` agent run now sets `metadata.skipUserMemoryAutoExtract: true` (a new per-run opt-out the hook honors via a new exported `readSkipAutoExtract(context)` in packages/memory/src/memory-auto-extract.ts тАФ early-returns before any extraction) AND `metadata.forbiddenToolNames: ["remember_fact"]` (defense in depth, via the existing exposure-layer block). Durable memory authoring stays with the explicit `muse remember` command (user-directed) and the conversational chat surface, whose auto-extraction is unchanged. Proof: 3 new memory unit tests in packages/memory/test/auto-extract-skip.test.ts (readSkipAutoExtract is true only when the flag is explicitly set; the hook writes NOTHING on an opted-out recall turn even when the extractor stub returns a fact-bearing payload; a normal/chat turn STILL extracts the fact тАФ so the skip is the ONLY behavior change, no chat regression) + LIVE on qwen3:8b: the exact `muse ask --with-tools` WireGuard probe that wrote `wireguard_default_mtu` before now leaves NO memory file across two runs, while P38-19's drift verdict still fires ("treat as unverified"). memory 30 files / 312 tests + autoconfigure 73 files / 484 tests + cli 166 files / 1761 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 тАФ a user who asks Muse a question can no longer have its general-knowledge answer silently turned into a fabricated "fact about you" that later recall presents as your own words тАФ P38-20 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Perception] Chat auto-memory no longer stores a fact the MODEL asserted as "what you told me" тАФ the provenance gate now covers the conversational surface (P38-21). P38-20 closed this on one-shot `muse ask` (by skipping extraction), and flagged the residual: the SAME leak lives on `muse chat`, through a SEPARATE extractor (`extractMemoryFromTurn` in apps/cli/src/chat-auto-memory.ts) that also mines the assistant reply тАФ so a user who ASKS "what's WireGuard's default MTU?" and gets "1420" would have `wireguard_default_mtu: 1420` silently saved as their OWN fact, which a later recall cites "ЁЯза from what you told me" (a fabricated provenance the user never stated). Fixed with a deterministic provenance gate (the same code-not-prompt shape as the citation gate): a new pure, exported `dropModelAssertedValues(record, userTurn, assistantOutput)` in packages/memory/src/memory-auto-extract.ts drops a fact/preference iff ALL of its DISTINCTIVE value tokens appear in the assistant's reply and NONE appear in the user's own turn тАФ i.e. the value was demonstrably the model's assertion, not the user's words. A value the user actually stated (its token is in their turn) survives; an inferred boolean like `allergy_penicillin: yes` survives because "yes" carries no distinctive token (fail-open тАФ un-attributable values are kept, not dropped); a malformed array-shaped payload is left untouched for the existing sanitizer. - [Perception/Grounding edge] `muse ask --file` refuses a BINARY file instead of hallucinating content from its garbled bytes (P37-14). Probing the ad-hoc `--file` perception source with a real-shaped binary PDF: `muse ask --file resume.pdf "what is this person's job title?"` read the PDF's raw bytes as UTF-8 (the handler did `readFile(path, "utf8")`), injected the garbage as note-class grounding, and the local model HALLUCINATED a confident answer тАФ "The resume file mentions 'Senior Software Engineer' [from resume.pdf]" тАФ citing a value that appears NOWHERE in the file (it was pure binary stream bytes). A sourced fabrication on the perception surface, exactly what the "shows its work" edge forbids. Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts: a new pure, exported `looksLikeBinaryContent(bytes)` (deterministic, zero deps тАФ a NUL byte is the canonical text-vs-binary signal; failing that, a >10% U+FFFD replacement-char ratio from a lossy UTF-8 decode of the first 8 KB) classifies the `--file` payload BEFORE it is grounded. A binary file is NOT injected as evidence; instead the user gets a clear "--file <path> looks like a binary file (PDF, image, office doc, тАж), not text тАФ I won't ground on it тАж extract the text first" message, and the answer honestly refuses rather than fabricating. A real text file is unaffected and still grounds + cites normally. - [Perception/Knowledge] `muse ask --file <pdf>` now READS the PDF and answers from its real text тАФ a user can ask Muse about a PDF directly, grounded + cited (P37-15). P37-14 made a binary `--file` refuse rather than hallucinate; this upgrades the most common "binary" case тАФ a PDF тАФ into a real capability. The `--file` handler now detects a PDF (`isPdfDocument`: a `.pdf` extension OR the `%PDF-` magic header) and extracts its text via `pdf-parse` (the SAME MIT, pure-JS reader `muse read` already ships тАФ no new dependency, and it's dynamically imported so it loads only when a PDF is actually read), then grounds + cites it `[from <file>.pdf]` like any note. A non-PDF binary (image, archive, office doc) still hits the P37-14 binary refusal; a scanned/empty-text PDF or a malformed PDF refuses honestly (no fabrication from garbage bytes); a plain text/markdown file is unchanged. - [Actuation] `muse remind`/`tasks`/`calendar` understand an English day-part word + a specific hour тАФ "tonight at 8", "tomorrow morning at 9", "this evening at 7" (P40-9). - [Perception/Knowledge] An HTML file is grounded on its readable TEXT (tags + script/style stripped, entities decoded), not raw tag-soup тАФ so `muse ask --file resume.html` / `muse read article.html` / `--file <folder-of-html>` work on HTML the way they do on text and PDFs (P37-17). Probing `--file` with an `.html` file exposed a real correctness defect: `muse ask --file resume.html "what is the email address?"` returned "jane&#64;globex.com" тАФ the HTML numeric entity `&#64;` (which is `@`) was never decoded, so the user got a MANGLED email тАФ and the ЁЯУО receipt showed raw `<html><head><style>тАж</style><script>тАж</script>` markup as the "source" (noisy, and it wastes the small model's context on tags/scripts). Root cause: every non-PDF `--file`/ingest path read the file bytes as UTF-8 verbatim, markup and all тАФ qwen coped with simple cases but the entities stayed mangled and large pages would bury the real content under markup. Fixed in apps/cli/src/document-reader.ts with a new pure, exported `htmlToText(html)` (regex-based, no DOM/parser dependency): it removes `<script>`/`<style>` blocks and HTML comments, strips the remaining tags, decodes the entities that actually corrupt grounded values (numeric `&#64;`, hex `&#x26;`, and the common named ones тАФ `&amp;`/`&lt;`/`&gt;`/`&quot;`/`&nbsp;`/`&mdash;`тАж), and collapses whitespace. `extractDocumentText` now routes `.html`/`.htm` through it, `.html`/`.htm` were added to `SUPPORTED_DOC_EXT` (so the directory walk for `muse read <dir>` / `muse ask --file <dir>` / `watch-folder --ingest` picks them up), and the single-`--file` path in commands-ask got the same branch (it has its own inline reader, applied AFTER the robust binary-refusal so a non-text binary is still refused). Proof: 4 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/document-reader.test.ts (`isHtmlDocument` matches .html/.htm not .txt; tags + `<script>`/`<style>` bodies stripped and whitespace collapsed; numeric/hex/named entities decoded тАФ `jane&#64;globex.com` тЖТ `jane@globex.com`, `a&#x26;b` тЖТ `a&b`, `Globex &amp; Co &mdash; 2026` тЖТ `Globex & Co тАФ 2026`; `extractDocumentText` reads an `.html` buffer as decoded text with no `<`) + the existing document-reader / read / notes-rag suites green + LIVE on qwen3:8b: `muse ask --file resume.html "what is the email address?"` now тЖТ "jane@globex.com" with a CLEAN text receipt ("Jane Doe Email: jane@globex.com Job title: Principal Engineer at Globex & Co."), `muse read article.html --save-to-notes` saves "VPN Setup The MTU should be set to 1380 for WireGuard." (clean, no tags), and `muse ask --file <dir>` over a folder containing the HTML grounds on it and cites `[from article.html]`. cli 167 files / 1782 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 тАФ a user can now point Muse at an HTML file or a folder of them (a saved web article, an exported resume) and get a cited answer from its actual readable text with values intact, instead of a markup-polluted, entity-mangled one тАФ P37-17 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Perception] A `[from <class>: тАж]` structured citation (commit / task / event / reminder / тАж) is no longer false-stripped тАФ the model's "from "-prefixed citation now survives the gate (P38-23). Probing the git-perception source (P37-11): `muse ask --git "what have I been working on recently?"` grounded on the user's real commits and answered correctly, citing a commit as `[from commit: feat(perception): muse ask grounds on the action log тАж]` тАФ but the citation gate then STRIPPED it with "тЪая╕П Removed 1 citation(s) to source(s) you don't have (commit: тАж) тАФ treat those claims as unverified" on a TRUE recall, making a correct git answer look unverified. Root cause: the local model frequently prepends the NOTE verb "from " to a STRUCTURED citation, but `enforceAnswerCitations`'s class regexes anchor on `[commit:` / `[task:` / `[event:` (with no "from "), and the note regex `[from <X>]` runs FIRST and mis-catches `[from commit: тАж]` as a non-existent note, stripping it before the commit handler ever sees it. Same defect class as P38-22 (contacts) and P38-17 (memory), now generalised across every structured citation class. - [Grounding edge/Perception] A past-SESSION recall cited by SLOT number ("[from session 1]") is no longer false-stripped тАФ the continuous-companion's "what did we discuss?" answers survive the gate (P38-24). - [Perception/Reach] `muse ask --url <url>` тАФ a user can now ask Muse about a public WEB PAGE, grounded on its readable text and cited, without ingesting it (P37-18). This is a NEW capability (Reach growth), the web counterpart of `--file`: `muse ask --url https://example.com "what is this domain for?"` fetches the page, extracts its readable text, grounds the answer on it cited `[from <host>]`, and an off-topic question honestly refuses rather than inventing page content. It reuses the existing SSRF-guarded `fetchReadableUrl` helper from @muse/mcp (the same one `muse notes ingest --url` already uses) тАФ it permits PUBLIC hosts only, re-checks the host after any redirect (so a redirect can't smuggle in a private/internal address), enforces a 15s timeout, and extracts readable text from HTML тАФ so there is no new fetch or egress machinery and the local-first posture is unchanged (the MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY gate governs LLM/voice egress, not reading a public web page the user explicitly asked about, which `outbound-safety.md` permits as "Muse may read the world freely"). Implemented in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts: a new `--url <url>` option and a branch that narrates "ЁЯМР fetching <url>тАж", grounds the page's passages through the SAME `selectFilePassages` lexical ranking + char budget as `--file`, and cites the page by host via a new pure exported `urlGroundingSource(finalUrl)` (which strips a leading `www.`); a fetch failure (bad host, non-200, timeout, no readable text) prints a clear "could not fetch --url тАж тАФ I won't ground on it" message and is never silently grounded-on. - [Felt] The "empty notes" on-ramp stays silent when the query SUPPLIES its own grounding (`--file`/`--url`/`--git`/`--shell`) or the user has past sessions тАФ completing P35-9 (P35-10). - [Actuation] A BARE duration тАФ "2 hours", "30 minutes", "3 days", "2h", "a week" тАФ now parses as an offset from now across `remind`/`tasks`/`calendar`/`snooze`; the literal "in" is optional (P40-10). Probing the actuators surfaced a broad gap: `muse remind snooze <id> --in "2 hours"`, `muse remind add "30 minutes" "call mom"`, and `muse tasks add "review" --due "3 days"` ALL failed with "dueAt must be an ISO-8601 timestamp or a supported relative phrase" тАФ every bare duration was rejected, and ONLY the form WITH the literal word "in" ("in 2 hours") parsed. This is especially awkward for `--in "2 hours"`, where the word "in" is already in the flag name so repeating it ("--in 'in 2 hours'") reads wrong, and "in 2 hours" is one of the most natural ways a person states a reminder time. Root cause: the two duration handlers in packages/mcp/src/loopback-relative-time.ts тАФ the full-word "in N <unit>" form and the compact "in Nh/Nm/Nd/Nw" form тАФ both hard-required a leading `in\s+`. Fixed by making that prefix optional (`(?:in\s+)?`) in both regexes, so a bare "2 hours" / "30 minutes" / "3 days" / "a week" / "2h" / "90 mins" / "2w" now reads as that offset from the current time. The change is purely additive тАФ a bare duration was previously unrecognised, so nothing that parsed before changes тАФ and it preserves the existing disambiguation: a bare number with NO unit ("5") still means a 24-hour clock hour (today 05:00, not "5 of something"), and an unknown unit ("3 horses") still rejects, so there are no false positives. Proof: 4 new parser unit tests in packages/mcp/test/relative-time-period.test.ts (bare full-word durations 2 hours/30 minutes/3 days/a week and bare compact 2h/90m/2d/2w each equal their explicit "in тАж" form; "5" stays a clock hour; "3 horses" rejected) + the single mcp.test.ts assertion that had codified the OLD "a bare 1h is rejected" behavior updated to the new intended parse + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1330 tests) + the cli remind/tasks suites green (38) + LIVE on the loop PC: `muse remind snooze <id> --in "2 hours"` тЖТ +2h, `muse remind add "30 minutes" t` тЖТ +30m, `muse tasks add "review" --due "3 days"` тЖТ +3 days, while "in 2 hours" and "5" (clock hour) are unregressed. mcp 167 files / 1330 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 тАФ a user can now write a reminder/task time the way they actually say it ("remind me in 2 hours" тЖТ just "2 hours", or `--in "2 hours"`) instead of being forced to include the literal word "in" тАФ P40-10 bullet

- [Grounding edge/Perception] The feed and contact grounding markers now embed the canonical `[feed: тАж]` / `[contact: тАж]` citation, so the local model cites them correctly INLINE тАФ fixing the root cause that the P38-22 (contact) and P38-25 (feed) post-hoc normalizers had only patched on the buffered copy (P38-28). Tracing WHY the model kept citing feeds and contacts in non-canonical forms (`[feed 1]` by slot, `[from contact_<uuid>]` by raw id) revealed an inconsistency in how the grounding context is built: the task, event, reminder, memory, and commit markers each embed the exact canonical citation inside the marker (`<<event N тАФ provider>>\n<title>\n[event: <title>]\n<<end>>`), which the small local model then copies verbatim тАФ but the feed marker (`<<feed N тАФ name (date)>>\n<title>тАж`) and the contact marker (`<<contact N тАФ id>>\n<name> тАФ <fields>`) did NOT include the `[feed: тАж]` / `[contact: тАж]` line, so the model improvised a slot number or the raw id. Because the default `muse ask` (chat-only) path STREAMS the model's raw output token-by-token and only normalizes the BUFFERED copy afterward (for the gate + receipt), the user saw the ugly `[feed 1]` / `[from contact_<uuid>]` inline even though the receipts were correct тАФ the prior fixes never touched the streamed text. Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts by adding `[feed: ${h.feedName}]` to the feed marker and `[contact: ${c.name}]` to the contact marker, matching the five markers that already embed their canonical citation; the P38-22/P38-24/P38-25 post-hoc normalizers remain as a safety net for the cases where the model still strays. - [Proactivity/Felt] Muse now notices the most common way you voice a commitment in passing тАФ "I'll тАж" / "I will тАж" / "I'm going to тАж" / "I'm gonna тАж" тАФ not just "I need to / have to / should" (P35-11). The SF-confidant "anticipates what you said you'd do" quality runs on the deterministic rule engine `detectUserCommitments` in packages/agent-core/src/commitment-detector.ts, which both `muse commitments scan` and `muse checkins scan` use to read recent chat (`~/.muse/last-chat.jsonl`) for things the user said they'd do and offer to track them / schedule a check-in. Its rules caught "I need to тАж", "I have/got to тАж", "I should тАж", and the Korean эХ┤ьХ╝/эХШъ╕░ыбЬ эЦИ forms тАФ but MISSED the single most common English way people state an intent: the future promise. A chat containing "I'll call the dentist tomorrow" or "I'm going to review the PR this afternoon" produced "No open commitments detected" тАФ Muse simply didn't see them. Fixed by adding two rules to the detector: `\bI(?:'ll|\s+will)\s+(тАж)` and `\bI(?:'m|\s+am)\s+(?:going\s+to|gonna)\s+(тАж)`, both mapped to a new `"will"` commitment kind at high confidence, with a small precision guard тАФ a `WILL_STATIVE_STARTERS` stoplist ({be, see, bet, say}) so a stative remark ("I'll be late", "I'll see", "I'll bet") is NOT mistaken for a task, and the existing interrogative filter still drops "Will I make it on time?" as a question. Proof: 2 new unit tests in packages/agent-core/test/commitment-detector.test.ts (all four intent forms тАФ I'll / I will / I'm going to / gonna тАФ detected as kind `will`/high; the stative and question forms detected as nothing) + the full @muse/agent-core suite green (112 files / 1399 tests, so the new kind broke no exhaustive consumer) + the cli build green + LIVE end-to-end on the loop PC: after seeding `~/.muse/last-chat.jsonl` with a user turn "Hey, I'll call the dentist tomorrow about the appointment", `muse commitments scan` now prints "Open commitments you mentioned (1): тАв call the dentist tomorrow about the appointment" (before this fix it reported "No open commitments detected in recent chat"). agent-core 112 files / 1399 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 тАФ a user who says "I'll do X" (the way most people actually phrase a commitment) now has Muse notice it and offer to track it, instead of it slipping by тАФ P35-11 bullet
- [Proactivity/Actuation] A commitment's follow-up check-in now fires AFTER the timeframe you stated, instead of always tomorrow at 10:00 (P35-12). P35-11 made Muse NOTICE a commitment voiced in passing; this hardens the next stage тАФ the proactive follow-up that actually arrives in the user's channel. `muse checkins scan` reads recent chat for things the user said they'd do (via `detectUserCommitments`) and schedules a warm "how did it go?" nudge for each (delivered at its due time by `runDueCheckins`). The defect: `scheduleCheckins` in packages/mcp/src/commitment-checkin.ts hardcoded EVERY check-in's due time to `now.getDate() + 1` at `slotHour` (tomorrow 10:00) тАФ so "submit the tax forms THIS WEEK" and "renew my passport NEXT WEEK" both got a follow-up the very next morning, a premature nag days before the user would plausibly have acted. This is exactly the real-world failure mode the human-directed focus calls a USER-FACING reliability defect (a proven-once actuator that misbehaves on a natural input), not inward churn. Fixed with a new pure exported `followupDayOffset(commitment)` that reads the timeframe the user voiced in the commitment text тАФ EN + KO тАФ and returns the day offset to fire the check-in PAST it: "next week" / "ыЛдьЭМ ьг╝" тЖТ 8, "this week" / "ьЭ┤ы▓И ьг╝" / "by <weekday>" тЖТ 5, "tomorrow" / "ыВ┤ьЭ╝" / "next <weekday>" тЖТ 2, and a same-day ("later today") or timeframe-less commitment тЖТ 1 (the previous next-day default, so nothing that worked before changes). The `due` Date is now computed per-commitment inside the schedule loop (it was a single value hoisted above the loop), and the default id factory switched from a `due`-derived suffix to the batch index so it no longer depends on the hoisted value. The follow-up timing is deterministic code (no model call тАФ the commitment detection is rule-only too), fail-safe (an unrecognised timeframe simply defaults to next-day, never drops the check-in). Proof: 2 new unit tests in packages/mcp/test/commitment-checkin.test.ts (`followupDayOffset` reads each EN+KO timeframe тАФ next weekтЖТ8, this week / ыЛдьЭМ┬╖ьЭ┤ы▓И ьг╝ / by fridayтЖТ5/8, tomorrow / ыВ┤ьЭ╝ / next thursdayтЖТ2, later today / no-timeframeтЖТ1; and `scheduleCheckins` over a "later today" + "this week" + "next week" batch yields three DISTINCT due dates +1/+5/+8) + the existing next-day, dedup, and maxPerDay scheduling tests still green + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1332 tests) + LIVE on the loop PC (today 2026-06-03): seeding `~/.muse/last-chat.jsonl` with "I'll email the team later today", "I need to submit the tax forms this week", "I have to renew my passport next week" and running `muse checkins scan` schedules them for 2026-06-04 / 2026-06-08 / 2026-06-11 10:00 respectively тАФ three distinct, timeframe-appropriate dates (before this fix all three were 2026-06-04 10:00, the same premature next-day slot). mcp 167 files / 1332 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 тАФ a user who says "I'll do X this week" is now followed up at the end of the week, not nagged the next morning тАФ P35-12 bullet
- [Grounding edge] The recall verdict's wrong-value escalation now catches a drifted EMAIL ADDRESS, not just a wrong number or named entity тАФ closing the most dangerous contact-data drift (P38-29). P38-2 made `verifyGroundingWithReverify` escalate a `grounded`-scoring answer that asserts a NUMBER ("MTU 9000" vs the note's 1380) or a capitalized NAMED ENTITY ("Dr. Lee" vs "Dr. Park") absent from the evidence to one fail-OPEN judge pass (claim-level grounding, since whole-answer coverage can't see a single wrong token). But an EMAIL ADDRESS escaped BOTH checks: the lexical tokenizer splits "jane@acme.com" into lowercase parts (jane/acme/com), so a drifted DOMAIN ("acme" where the note says "globex") is neither a pure digit nor a capitalized entity тАФ meaning a confident, high-coverage, fully-cited answer asserting a WRONG contact email read `grounded` and was handed to the user as fact (verified live: the wrong-email answer scores base verdict grounded at confidence 1.00 with NO gate). For a contact / outbound surface that is the single most dangerous fabrication тАФ Muse confidently gives you a wrong address you might then email. Fixed in packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts: `answerAssertsUnsupportedValue` now also extracts whole email addresses from the (citation-stripped) answer via `/[a-z0-9._%+-]+@[a-z0-9.-]+\.[a-z]{2,}/giu` and flags any not present VERBATIM in the joined raw evidence text (case-insensitive тАФ a real email is copied from a note, never reformatted), so a drifted email triggers the SAME fail-OPEN judge pass as a wrong number and is demoted to "I'm not sure" on an unsupported verdict. Scoped to emails (the clean, unambiguous, highest-value identifier; @handles/URLs deferred as noisier). Fail-open and zero-cost on the common path: a CORRECT email is present in evidence, so `emails.some(not-in-evidence)` is false and no extra judge pass fires тАФ only a genuinely drifted email pays for re-verification, and a judge error never demotes a correct answer. - [Perception] A user can now ground Muse on whatever text they just COPIED тАФ `muse ask --clipboard "<question>"` answers from the clipboard, cited `[from clipboard]`, with an honest refusal off-topic (P37-19). This is a NEW read-only local perception source, the ephemeral sibling of `--file` (a saved file) and `--url` (a web page): you copy an article, an error message, a code snippet, or an email, then ask Muse about it immediately тАФ no file to save first. It routes through the SAME cited-recall + grounding gate as `--file`/`--url` rather than bypassing it: the clipboard text is chunked by the existing `selectFilePassages` ranking into `scored`, so the answer passes `enforceAnswerCitations` (only real sources cited) and the `groundingVerdictNotice` rubric, and an off-topic question gets the honest "I don't have that" refusal тАФ a NEW surface that is gated by construction (the user-locked "gate a new surface" done as perception growth, not another citation tweak). Implemented as a new leaf module apps/cli/src/clipboard-reader.ts: a pure, exported `clipboardCommand(platform)` that maps the OS to its standard clipboard tool (darwin тЖТ `pbpaste`, win32 тЖТ PowerShell `Get-Clipboard`, linux тЖТ `xclip -selection clipboard -o`, any other platform тЖТ undefined) and a `readClipboardText(platform?)` shim that shells out via `execFile` тАФ read-only and entirely local (the clipboard text never leaves the machine, consistent with MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY: this is a local read, not LLM egress). - [Grounding edge] The "shows its work" source receipt is now suppressed when the answer FAILS the grounding verdict, so the edge never vouches for a fabrication (P38-30). Falsifying P37-19 (`muse ask --clipboard`) surfaced a general edge-integrity hole on the chat-only ask path: the source receipt ("ЁЯУО From your notes (open to verify): тАв from clipboard тАФ '<chunk>'") was printed UNCONDITIONALLY and BEFORE the grounding verdict ran. So an off-topic question that the local model answered from its own parametric knowledge and cited to the grounded source тАФ e.g. over a clipboard holding a printer IP, "who won the 2018 world cup?" тЖТ "The 2018 World Cup was won by France [from clipboard]" тАФ got BOTH a receipt that appeared to vouch for it AND a contradictory "тЪая╕П Grounding check: тАж treat as unverified" warning beneath. The receipt is the edge's flagship "shows its work" artifact; rendering it on an answer that failed its OWN grounding check lends false authority to precisely the un-groundable claim the edge promises to drop, and the two outputs (receipt says "grounded on clipboard", warning says "not backed") directly contradict. An ungrounded answer shows the warning (and `--repair` suggestion) ALONE, with no misleading receipt; a genuinely grounded answer keeps its full followable receipt unchanged. This affects EVERY grounding source (notes / `--file` / `--url` / `--clipboard` / contacts / tasks / events / reminders / sessions / feeds / memory / commands / commits / actions), not just the clipboard case that surfaced it. The change is a pure reorder + one guard тАФ no new machinery, no second model call, deterministic.
