- [Reliability/Actuation] A hung or unresponsive Google Calendar endpoint can no longer block Muse indefinitely тАФ every Google Calendar HTTP call (the API requests AND the OAuth token refresh) now has a per-attempt request TIMEOUT (AbortController, default 15s), so a slow/stalled third party fails fast with a clear error instead of stalling `muse calendar` / the agent run (P41 actuator hardening тАФ the timeout dimension of "daily-reliable actuators"; ACT axis). The messaging providers (Telegram / Discord / Slack / LINE via `fetchWithTimeout`) and the Gmail provider (`fetchWithRetry`, 15s AbortController) already bounded their requests, but `GoogleCalendarProvider` called `this.fetchImpl(...)` RAW at both fetch sites тАФ with no timeout/AbortSignal тАФ so a hung Google endpoint (a network black-hole, an unresponsive proxy, a stalled TLS handshake) blocked the call until the OS socket timeout (often minutes). That genuinely STALLS the caller: the agent's wallclock cap (`maxRunWallclockMs`) only checks BETWEEN tool iterations, never mid-fetch, and the `muse brief` / daemon calendar reads have no other guard. Added a `timeoutMs` option (`GoogleCalendarRetryOptions`, default 15000, 0 disables) + a private `fetchWithTimeout(url, init)` that races each fetch against an `AbortController` timer (clearing it in `finally`) and routes both the API path and the token-refresh path through it. SAFE by construction via the EXISTING retry seam: a timeout rejects тЖТ the request method's network-failure `catch` decides by idempotency тАФ an idempotent GET retries (`networkRetries = this.retries`) so a flaky moment doesn't drop the calendar from the briefing, while a WRITE (POST/PATCH/DELETE) has `networkRetries = 0` so a timed-out mutation is NEVER retried (a timeout is ambiguous тАФ the write may have committed тАФ so a retry could double-act; this preserves the same no-double-act guarantee as the 429-only write-retry). Proof: 2 new contract-faithful tests (a real hung-endpoint fake тАФ the API fetch returns a promise that only the injected AbortController resolves, by rejecting on `signal`; the token endpoint responds normally; never a fake registry) in packages/calendar/test/google-provider.test.ts тАФ a hung GET is aborted on each attempt and retried then thrown (`timed out`, asserted abort count = initial + 1 retry = 2, idempotent), and a hung WRITE is aborted EXACTLY ONCE and thrown (abort count = 1 тАФ never retried, no double-act) тАФ plus the full @muse/calendar suite green (12 files / 139 tests, the existing OAuth / 429-retry / 5xx / malformed-body / event-mapping contract tests unchanged), calendar tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0. HTTP-actuator reliability slice (no model) тЖТ the contract-faithful hung-endpoint fake is the surface check, not smoke:live. calendar 12/139 + pnpm lint 0/0 тАФ a slow or black-holed Google Calendar can no longer hang Muse's morning brief or calendar actuator; the calendar provider reaches request-timeout parity with messaging + email, with double-act still fenced off (write timeouts never retry) тАФ P41 (ACT-axis actuator hardening, request timeout, Google Calendar)
- [Reliability/Actuation] A multi-step `muse ask --with-tools` task now ADAPTS when a read/lookup step fails non-recoverably тАФ instead of giving up, the plan-execute loop RE-DECOMPOSES: it asks the model for an ALTERNATIVE read-only approach to the same intent and runs it, so a task carries to a verified done via a different route (P43-2 carry-to-done, the "replans on a failed step" leg now real; ACT axis тАФ a 13-agent panel + 3-attacker red-team chose this as the highest-value SAFELY-achievable big lever, over encryption-at-rest [its first slice was red-teamed as a data-loss/race risk] and autonomous graduation [already shipped + sign-safe, no new code]). Slices 1тАУ2 added the per-step post-condition (`classifyStepEffect`) + a bounded read-step RETRY, but a step that failed even after retry was simply marked failed тАФ the loop ran once top-to-bottom with no adaptive re-routing. Added `replanFailedReadStep` (packages/agent-core/src/plan-execute-loop.ts): when a READ step's effect fails after the bounded retry, it builds a focused re-plan prompt (the original request + the failed step + its reason), generates an alternative plan over ONLY the read-risk tools (`generatePlan` with read-tool descriptions), and runs up to `PLAN_REPLAN_MAX_STEPS=2` alternative steps тАФ the first that COMPLETES with a passing post-condition recovers the step's intent (recorded as `"<desc> (recovered via <tool>)"`). CRITICAL SAFETY (the reason the panel chose this as the SAFE lever, and the red-team's required guard): recovery is READ-ONLY and can NEVER double-act тАФ (1) only a read-risk step failure triggers a re-plan (`retryable`), a WRITE/execute failure is NEVER replanned because the mutation may have committed (outbound-safety.md), and (2) the alternative plan is FILTERED to read-risk tool names тАФ any write/execute step the model proposes in the re-plan is DROPPED, not executed; the immutable `executed[]` is never re-run, so a completed non-idempotent step can't repeat. The happy path is untouched (a succeeding step never replans тЖТ zero added latency in the common case); the re-plan model call fires ONLY on a read-step failure, bounded by `maxToolCalls`. Proof: 3 new contract-faithful tests (a scripted runner giving precise control of the plan/re-plan model responses + each tool result, no live model) in packages/agent-core/test/plan-execute-replan.test.ts тАФ a failed READ step RECOVERS via an alternative read tool (retried ├Ч2 then the alternative runs, step flips to success, carries to synthesis, exactly ONE re-plan); a failed WRITE step is NEVER re-planned (executed exactly once, zero re-plan model calls тАФ no double-act); and a re-plan that proposes a WRITE step has it DROPPED (the write tool is never called, the read step stays failed) тАФ plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (113 files / 1430 tests; the existing partial-failure synthesis test updated to find its synthesis request by content since the re-plan adds a model call), agent-core tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE regression on the loop PC: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (background-review-e2e exercises the agent runtime тАФ the additive re-plan, which only fires on a read-step failure the batteries don't hit, regressed nothing). agent-core 113/1430 + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 тАФ a multi-step task no longer dies when a lookup step has no working answer; it adaptively re-routes to an alternative read, with double-act fenced off by construction (read-only re-plan, write failures never replanned) тАФ P43-2 (ACT-axis carry-to-done, adaptive read-only re-decomposition, panel-chosen + red-teamed)
- [Trust/Privacy] A user can now ENCRYPT their user-memory AT REST тАФ `muse memory encrypt` rewrites `~/.muse/user-memory.json` (the confided life: facts, preferences, the typed user model) as an AES-256-GCM envelope, so a stolen/seized laptop or a leaked backup can no longer read it; reads/writes stay transparent (the agent's persona still loads it), with `muse memory decrypt` to reverse and `muse memory encryption-status` to check тАФ making "it can't tell anyone" true against STORAGE access, not just network egress (NEW Trust axis; the discretion-refusal half of the identity promise. Decided + safety-designed by a 13-agent panel that chose this lever, then a 3-attacker red-team of the actual diff that FOUND + drove a fix for a cross-process data-loss race before commit). Until now notes/memory/episodes/action-log were PLAINTEXT JSON behind OS file-perms only тАФ only credentials/exports were encrypted тАФ so the most sensitive store (what Muse knows about you) sat readable on disk. Added `packages/memory/src/memory-encryption.ts` (AES-256-GCM + scrypt-derived key, mirroring the proven credential-store envelope; the key is `MUSE_MEMORY_KEY` or a per-host fallback) and wired it into `FileUserMemoryStore` behind the red-team's REQUIRED GUARDS, each tested: (1) the read path NEVER writes тАФ it decrypts-or-reads-plaintext and returns the format, so there is no encrypt-on-read race; (2) FAIL-CLOSED-WITHOUT-DESTRUCTION тАФ a WRONG key (or a per-host key changed by a machine rename, or tampering) THROWS a clear error and leaves the ciphertext byte-UNCHANGED, and because every write reads-first, a write under the wrong key also throws (it can never bury the ciphertext with empty data); (3) the one-shot `encryptAtRest()` writes a `.plaintext-backup-<ts>` BEFORE encrypting (recovery if the key derivation ever changes); (4) the un-migrated plaintext path is byte-unchanged (opt-in). The red-team's CRITICAL finding тАФ the per-process write mutex + a migration-only lock let a daemon `upsertFact` in one process race a CLI `encrypt` in another (read-modify-write, last-rename-wins тЖТ a fact or the encryption lost) тАФ was FIXED before commit: ALL writes (upsert / delete / encrypt / decrypt) now serialize through ONE cross-process O_EXCL `.lock`, with stale-lock STEALING (an mtime > 30s lock from a crashed writer is reclaimed) so a crash can't block writes forever, while reads stay lock-free (the atomic rename keeps a concurrent reader consistent). Proof: ~12 new deterministic tests (no model) тАФ the crypto primitive round-trips + THROWS on a wrong key; the store round-trips (cleartext absent on disk, reads decrypt, writes preserve the encrypted format), writes the plaintext backup, FAILS CLOSED on a wrong key with the ciphertext byte-unchanged (the killer data-loss case) including the wrong-key WRITE not burying it, read() never writes, decrypt reverses, and a stale lock is stolen (packages/memory/test/memory-user-store-file.test.ts); plus the full @muse/memory suite green (31 files / 329 tests), @muse/cli green (170 files / 1870 tests), memory+cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE end-to-end on the loop PC: `muse memory encrypt` over a seeded store removed the confided secret from cleartext on disk (0 hits, AES envelope), kept a recoverable plaintext backup, `encryption-status` reported encrypted, a WRONG key failed closed ("the encrypted data is intact on disk... restore the .plaintext-backup"), and `muse memory decrypt` restored the plaintext тАФ the lockfile released cleanly (no leftover). memory 31/329 + cli 170/1870 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse memory encrypt/decrypt` тАФ the confided life can now be encrypted at rest, fail-closed and race-safe, so a stolen device can't read it; the discretion refusal is real against storage, not just the network тАФ P44 (Trust/privacy, user-memory encryption-at-rest, panel-decided + red-teamed)
- [Trust/Privacy] A user can now ENCRYPT their session-history AT REST тАФ `muse episode encrypt` rewrites `~/.muse/episodes.json` (the auto-captured prior-session summaries: what you talked about, decided, asked Muse to follow up on) as an AES-256-GCM envelope under the SAME `MUSE_MEMORY_KEY` as user-memory (ONE key for the whole confided life), so a stolen/seized laptop or a leaked backup can't read your session history either; reads stay transparent (`muse episode list` / the persona surfacing still decrypt), with `muse episode decrypt` to reverse and `muse episode encryption-status` to check (extends the P44 Trust axis from user-memory to the episodes store тАФ the discretion-refusal half of "it can't tell anyone", now over a second confided store). P44-1 encrypted user-memory; episodes/action-log were still PLAINTEXT JSON behind OS file-perms only. Built a REUSABLE `encrypted-file` helper (packages/mcp/src/encrypted-file.ts: `readMaybeEncrypted` / `writeMaybeEncrypted` / `isFileEncryptedAtRest` / `withFileLock` / `encryptFileAtRest` / `decryptFileAtRest`) reusing `@muse/memory`'s proven AES-256-GCM envelope, and wired it into the function-based episodes store (packages/mcp/src/personal-episodes-store.ts): `readEpisodes` decrypts fail-closed (a wrong key THROWS and is NEVER quarantined-to-empty тАФ an undecryptable store is not corrupt; the non-JSON plaintext corrupt-quarantine path is preserved), `writeEpisodes` peeks the on-disk format and rewrites in the SAME format under a cross-process O_EXCL lock the migration also takes (so an ordinary write can't race `encryptEpisodesAtRest` and clobber it), and `encryptEpisodesAtRest` writes a `.plaintext-backup-<ts>` before migrating + seeds an empty encrypted file when the store is absent (so future episodes stay encrypted). Then a 3-attacker red-team OF THE ACTUAL DIFF (concurrency / fail-closed / regression lenses, per "build тЖТ red-team the DIFF тЖТ fix тЖТ commit") drove FOUR pre-commit fixes: (1) `writeMaybeEncrypted` now delegates to the hardened `atomicWriteFile` (randomUUID tmp suffix so same-ms writers don't collide on rename; fsync before rename тАФ a torn ENCRYPTED file would be an undecryptable lock-out, not just empty); (2) `withFileLock` now stamps a per-holder NONCE and removes the lock ONLY if it still holds that nonce, so a >30s-slow holder whose lock was stolen mid-flight can't delete the new holder's lock (no orphan-cascade / third concurrent writer); (3) the `muse episode encrypt` output now DISCLOSES the plaintext backup is CLEARTEXT to delete once the key is confirmed (the red-team's strongest finding тАФ an undisclosed full-cleartext sibling defeats at-rest confidentiality); (4) the three new subcommands got automated CLI tests. Proof: 15 new deterministic store tests (no model) тАФ round-trip (cleartext absent on disk, reads decrypt), format preserved on subsequent writes, empty/absent-store seeds encrypted, plaintext backup holds the originals, idempotent re-encrypt, FAILS CLOSED on a wrong key with the ciphertext byte-UNCHANGED (incl. a wrong-key WRITE that can't bury it), read() never writes (bytes + mtime unchanged), decrypt reverses, decrypt-wrong-key fails closed, status is format-only (no key), corrupt-plaintext still quarantines, a STALE lock is stolen, 20 concurrent upserts on an encrypted store all survive + stay encrypted, clear preserves the format (packages/mcp/test/episodes-encryption.test.ts) + 4 new CLI tests driving the real subcommands through commander (statusтЖТencryptтЖТstatusтЖТlist, wrong-key fail-closed, decrypt-reverts, --json) (apps/cli/src/commands-episode-encryption.test.ts); plus the full @muse/mcp suite green (169 files / 1397 tests), @muse/cli green (171 files / 1874 tests), mcp+cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE end-to-end on the loop PC: `muse episode encrypt` over a seeded store left an AES-256-GCM envelope (0 plaintext leak, cleartext-backup warning shown, NO orphan `.lock` left behind), `muse episode list` decrypted transparently, a WRONG key failed closed with the data intact, and `muse episode decrypt` restored the plaintext. mcp 169/1397 + cli 171/1874 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse episode encrypt/list/decrypt` тАФ a second confided store (your session history) can now be encrypted at rest, fail-closed and race-safe, on a reusable helper ready for action-log next; the discretion refusal now covers what you said to Muse, not just what it learned about you тАФ P44-2 (Trust/privacy, episodes encryption-at-rest, reusable helper, panel-pattern + red-teamed)
- [Trust/Accountability] A user can now run `muse actions --verify` and get a DETERMINISTIC proof that the autonomous-action audit log (`~/.muse/action-log.json` тАФ what Muse did on their behalf: what/why/when/result) was not silently deleted, reordered, edited, or backdated тАФ and if it WAS, the exact entry index where the chain first breaks (exit 1 so a cron/script can gate on it). This capability did not exist: the log was "append-only BY CONTRACT" (personal-action-log-store.ts docstring) with ZERO integrity linkage тАФ a buggy concurrent writer, a partial-write crash, or any process with file access could rewrite history undetectably, so the accountability leg of "Tell it everything. It can't tell anyone." was unfalsifiable. Made it tamper-EVIDENT with a Merkle hash-chain (Haber-Stornetta 1991; RFC 6962): added `prevHash?: string` to ActionLogEntry (optional тЖТ legacy logs stay readable), a pure `computeEntryHash(entry, prevHash)` = SHA-256 over the entry's canonical content (id/userId/when/what/why/result/objectiveId/detail, prevHash EXCLUDED from its own body) bound to the prior hash, so a one-byte change to any historical entry diverges its hash тАФ which is the NEXT entry's prevHash тАФ cascading the break to the tip; `appendActionLog` now seals each new entry to `chainTipHash(existing)` (genesis for the first; the per-file append queue keeps the chain fork-free under concurrency); `verifyActionLogChain(entries)` (pure) walks the STORED/append order recomputing every link and returns `{ok, brokenAtIndex, reason, linkedEntries}`, treating leading legacy (no-prevHash) entries as a valid pre-chain prefix and a missing link AFTER the chain began as a break; `verifyActionLogChainFile(file)` reads via readActionLog (append order, NOT queryActionLog which re-sorts newest-first). Wired `--verify` into `muse actions` (commands-actions.ts) before the query path: "тЬУ chain intact тАФ N linked" or "тЬЧ TAMPERING DETECTED at entry N: тАж" + `command.error(exitCode:1)`. HONEST framing baked into the copy + docstring: tamper-EVIDENT (catches accidental/partial-write/external-process/non-recomputing mutation), NEVER tamper-PROOF (a motivated attacker who recomputes the whole chain needs an off-box anchor тАФ out of scope). This slice was chosen by the cross-domain ideation panel (info-theory/distributed-systems) AFTER the bio panel's top pick тАФ an immune-system NEGATIVE-SELECTION per-claim grounding detector тАФ was BUILT and then FALSIFIED by a live nomic-embed calibration: recombination hallucinations (real entities, wrong combination) embed nearest-self at 0.79тАУ0.85 vs faithful claims at 0.80тАУ0.81 (the embedding is topical, not propositional), so it could not beat the existing lexical+value gate on its own falsifiable kill condition тАФ reverted, not shipped (an honest negative result; the "shows its work" discipline applied to my own work). Proof: 11 new deterministic mcp unit tests (no model) тАФ appendтЖТverify intact (first entry chains to genesis, each to its predecessor); in-place edit caught at the next link; deleted-middle / reordered / backdated-`when` each detected at the precise index; legacy no-prevHash entries verify as an intact prefix; a new append onto a legacy log starts a verifiable chain from the legacy tip; a prevHash stripped mid-chain is a break; empty/missing log vacuously intact (packages/mcp/test/action-log-chain.test.ts) + 3 new CLI tests (intact log prints "chain intact"; a byte-flipped on-disk entry exits 1 naming the broken index; --verify --json emits the structured verdict тАФ apps/cli/src/commands-actions.test.ts); plus the full @muse/mcp suite green (170 files / 1407 tests, the existing serialize/concurrency tests confirm back-compat), @muse/cli green (171 files / 1877 tests), `pnpm check` exit 0 across ALL workspaces (mcp interface change consumed by cli + api), `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE end-to-end on the built CLI (deterministic SHA-256, no Ollama): a 3-action chain verified "тЬУ chain intact тАФ 3 linked entries verified" (exit 0), then a silently-DELETED middle action was caught "тЬЧ TAMPERING DETECTED at entry 1 тАж does not chain to entry 0" (exit 1) and a BACKDATED `when` was caught at its exact index (exit 1). mcp 170/1407 + cli 171/1877 + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse actions --verify` (intact + deletion + backdate) тАФ the audit trail of what Muse did on your behalf is now tamper-evident, closing the accountability leg of the trust moat; no model needed, so the proof is fully deterministic тАФ P44-3 (Trust/accountability, tamper-evident action-log hash-chain, cross-domain panel pick after the bio top-pick was live-falsified)
- [Reach/Trust] A user can now run a GROUNDED swarm council тАФ set `MUSE_A2A_COUNCIL_GROUNDED=true` and a council member (your own Muse's voice AND any peer that opted in) self-ABSTAINS, staying silent, when its OWN notes hold no CONFIDENT evidence for the question, so an ignorant peer can't dilute the synthesis with a confident-but-ungrounded opinion (the classic multiagent-debate failure mode). This is the multi-agent twin of "I'm not sure" тАФ it extends the fabrication=0 grounding invariant to a FIFTH surface (the peer DRAFT) at the COLONY level, and it's the structural prerequisite for honest colony learning (who SPEAKS on a question reveals who has corpus for it тАФ emergent specialization/federated trust need members to first stop speaking when ignorant). Chosen by the multi-angle ideation's technical-edge panel (3-lens red-teamed; it REJECTED Federated Strategy-Reward as unsafe тАФ that needs a peer-messageтЖТlocal-state write punching a hole in inbound-inert). DESIGN: deliberately OPT-IN per node (the default council stays full deliberation тАФ abstaining-by-default would gut its main use, opinion questions like "rent or buy" where no one has corpus); purely SUBTRACTIVE (members say LESS, never more тЖТ strengthens the trust core); entirely LOCAL (the corpus NEVER crosses the wire тАФ only the abstain/speak decision does, so no new shareable kind, inbound-inert untouched); and the gate is DETERMINISTIC (CRAG retrieval-confidence verdict, `classifyRetrievalConfidence`, not the stochastic 8B тАФ so qwen can't flake it). Built `abstainIfUngrounded(draft, matches, opts)` (speak only on a `confident` corpus match; `none`/`ambiguous` abstains тАФ keyed on RETRIEVAL confidence not draft token-coverage, since the council reasons in GENERAL terms by design so a coverage gate would silence everyone тАФ the over-abstention failure) + `produceGroundedCouncilReasoning` (short-circuits to abstain with NO model call when the corpus isn't confident) in packages/agent-core/src/council.ts; a `councilCorpusMatches` helper (apps/cli/src/council-corpus.ts) that reuses the precomputed notes index + the SAME absolute cosine the recall wedge grades by, fail-CLOSED to silence (empty тЗТ abstain) when there's no index or the embedder is down; wired into BOTH the `muse swarm council` initiator's own voice (round 1 + debate rounds) AND the `muse swarm serve` responder (this-Muse-as-a-peer), so the whole colony respects the posture; surfaced in `muse swarm status`. NOTE the real design insight that shaped it: the council is DELIBERATION not RECALL, so self-abstention is opt-in тАФ this avoided shipping a feature that would have broken the council's primary use. Proof: 7 new deterministic agent-core unit tests (no model) тАФ abstainIfUngrounded speaks on confident / abstains on ambiguous+none+empty-draft / honors a custom confidentAt; produceGroundedCouncilReasoning SHORT-CIRCUITS (asserts NO model request spent) when not confident and reasons when confident; an end-to-end selectivity test that an abstaining member is absent from the synthesised contributors (packages/agent-core/test/council.test.ts) + 5 new CLI unit tests for councilCorpusMatches (no index тЖТ []; ranks own chunks by absolute cosine тЖТ confident in-corpus; off-corpus тЖТ not confident; embedder-throws тЖТ fail-closed []; env parsing) (apps/cli/src/council-corpus.test.ts) + the SwarmStatus grounded-posture render; plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (113 files / 1438 tests), @muse/cli green (173 files / 1887 tests), `pnpm check` exit 0 across ALL workspaces (agent-core council change consumed by cli + api), `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE battery on the loop PC (qwen3:8b + real nomic-embed) тАФ `verify-council-self-abstention` (now in `eval:self-improving`, 19 batteries): an off-corpus question (top cosine 0.467, ambiguous) made the member ABSTAIN, an in-corpus question (top cosine 0.621, confident тАФ the over-abstention TRIPWIRE) made it SPEAK, and the council synthesised contributors `["alice"]` with the abstainer `bob` EXCLUDED; the two existing council batteries (`verify-council`, `verify-council-grounding`) still PASS (no regression). agent-core 113/1438 + cli 173/1887 + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live verify-council-self-abstention (real qwen+nomic-embed: abstain/speak/exclude all proven) тАФ Muse's private swarm now has an honest colony floor: an ignorant peer stays silent instead of voting confidently, the 5th grounded surface, and the substrate every richer colony-learning step needs тАФ A2A-6 (Reach/Trust, council self-abstention, technical-edge panel pick, the colony-learning frontier)
- [Grounding edge/Front-door] A user can now run `muse ask --why` and, when Muse refuses or flags an answer, SEE exactly why тАФ which deterministic grounding criterion fell short and the measured value vs its threshold тАФ turning an opaque "I'm not sure" into an inspectable, ACTIONABLE judgement (rephrase, reindex, or add a note). This is the "shows its work" moat applied to the REFUSAL itself: the recall wedge already refuses instead of guessing, but the refusal was a black box; now `--why` names the failing rubric criterion(s) тАФ "no notes came close enough (best match 0.42, I need 0.55) тАФ confidence criterion", "the evidence covers only 6% of the answer's wording (I need 50%) тАФ coverage criterion", "your notes address only 0% of the question (I need 34%) тАФ answerability criterion", or "the answer cited N source(s) you don't have (тАж) тАФ citation criterion". The moat-analysis ideation workflow's red-teamed pick (chosen as the differentiating front-door slice): a refusal-WITH-REASONS is structurally uncopyable by hermes/openclaw тАФ their capability-first design has no refusal and no per-criterion verdict to surface, while Muse's deterministic 4-criterion `verifyGrounding` rubric is exactly the hard-to-replicate asset. Built a pure `explainGroundingVerdict(verification, { topCosine, confidentAt, coverageFloor, answerabilityFloor })` in packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts that reads the rubric `verifyGrounding` ALREADY computes (the rubric stores the categorical confidence, so the caller passes the top match's raw cosine for the "best match 0.42" line) + `verification.reason`/`invalidCitations`, and emits 1тАУ4 plain-language lines naming every criterion below its floor; returns `[]` for a `grounded` verdict (SILENT on the happy path тАФ a targeted trust affordance, not a debug firehose). Wired `--why` into `muse ask` (commands-ask.ts) AFTER the verdict block, isolated from the repair flow: NO extra model call (the rubric is deterministic), gated to stderr (`!--json`), and it runs even on a REFUSAL (which the fabrication warning deliberately skips, since a refusal asserts no claim) because explaining WHY it refused is exactly the point. Proof: 6 new deterministic agent-core unit tests (no model) тАФ a grounded verdict yields []; a no-retrieval verdict names the confidence criterion with "best match 0.42, I need 0.55"; an off-evidence answer names the coverage criterion with the measured %; a fabricated `[from ghost.md]` names the citation criterion + lists the source; an ambiguous-retrieval answer is flagged "loosely related тАФ confidence criterion (low)"; custom thresholds render in the explanation (packages/agent-core/test/explain-grounding-verdict.test.ts); plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (114 files / 1444 tests), @muse/cli build clean, `pnpm check` exit 0 across ALL workspaces (the agent-core export consumed by cli + api), `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE run on the loop PC (qwen3:8b + real nomic-embed): `muse ask --why "what is the best sourdough bread recipe?"` over a VPN-only notes corpus REFUSED ("I am not sure, sirтАж") and printed "ЁЯФО Why I can't answer from your notes: тАв the evidence covers only 6% of the answer's wording (I need 50%) тАФ coverage criterion тАв your notes address only 0% of the question (I need 34%) тАФ answerability criterion". agent-core 114/1444 + cli build clean + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse ask --why` (off-corpus refusal explained) тАФ Muse's refusal is no longer a black box; the user sees which criterion failed and by how much, on the everyday front-door surface, which is the moat ("shows its work") made tangible where hermes/openclaw structurally can't follow тАФ P38-35 (Grounding edge/front-door, the --why refusal trace, moat-analysis panel pick)
- [Knowledge/Perception] A user can now have `muse ask` FOLLOW their `[[wiki-links]]` тАФ graph-augmented recall on the front door: an ask answer can ground on a note 1-hop LINKED from the matching note but whose own text didn't match the query, so the answer-bearing note your Zettelkasten points to (that the embedding ranking alone misses) reaches the model (HippoRAG / GraphRAG, Edge et al. 2024). Until now the note-link graph helped only `muse recall --expand` (1-hop); the front-door `muse ask` ignored it, so a question whose answer lived in a LINKED-but-non-matching note would refuse or under-ground. - [Self-improve/Felt] A preference you TAUGHT Muse can no longer silently vanish тАФ when the background daemon's disuse-decay tick fades a positively-reinforced strategy across the healthyтЖТnear-forgotten line (reward >1 тЖТ тЙд1) purely because you stopped using it, the daemon now DELIVERS a rescue notice to your channel ("A preference you taught me тАФ '<strategy>' тАФ is fading from disuse. - [Reach/Reliability] A message a user CONFIRMS now survives a transient rate-limit instead of being dropped тАФ the draft-first outbound send (`muse messaging send` + the agent's `muse.messaging.send` tool, both routing through `sendMessageWithApproval`) rides the same `sendWithRetry` ladder the background notices already use, so a one-off `429 + Retry-After` (or a transient 5xx) is waited-out and the message is delivered, instead of being logged `failed` and lost on the first blip. - [Self-improve/Autonomy] A correction you make now AUTONOMOUSLY stops Muse applying a contradicted preference in LATER sessions тАФ the daemon, unattended, classifies each new correction against the strategies Muse currently applies and SUBTRACTIVELY decays the ones it CONTRADICTS, so "a correction in session A changes session B" closes the loop SIGN-SAFE. This FLIPS P43-1 (THE #1 lever, the last open P43 bullet тАФ the autonomous self-development daemon) and was the explicitly-held injection-path change: the decide-and-do directive (2026-06-04) said stop deferring the big levers to Jinan тАФ judge + DO it. The blocker was a genuine sign-error risk: a correction is a NEGATIVE signal and lexical topic-overlap can't tell "do X" from "STOP X", so decaying/graduating on a Jaccard match inverts the user's signal. The unblock is an LLM polarity gate `classifyCorrectionContradiction` (packages/agent-core/src/correction-distiller.ts) тАФ LIVE-validated 11/11 with ZERO false-CONTRADICT on qwen3:8b, including the exact topic-overlap-but-opposite cases ("stop using a warm sign-off" vs "use a warm sign-off" тЖТ CONTRADICT) a lexical matcher misses тАФ wired into `eval:self-improving` as a permanent regression battery (apps/cli/scripts/verify-correction-polarity.mjs). The daemon's self-learn tick (apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.ts), after distilling this tick's new corrections into probation lessons, runs `decayContradictedStrategies` (packages/autoconfigure/src/decay-contradicted.ts): for each new correction ├Ч each INJECTED strategy, on a confident `contradict` it drops that strategy's reward to the avoid floor (PLAYBOOK_AVOID_BELOW = -4 тЖТ `isInjectableStrategy` false тЖТ no longer applied; reversible тАФ a `muse playbook reward` lifts it back), and delivers a felt notice to the user's channel ("You corrected me, so I've stopped applying '<strategy>' going forward. If that was wrong, reinforce it with `muse playbook reward <id>`."). SAFE BY CONSTRUCTION тАФ the sign-error the playbook panel feared is STRUCTURALLY impossible: DECAY-ONLY (it NEVER graduates a probation guess, NEVER raises a reward, NEVER clears probation тАФ the ADDITIVE auto-graduation stays bound to a manual positive act, as the 10-voter panel ratified), so the worst case of a polarity error is a recoverable wrongly-avoided strategy, NEVER an autonomous fabrication entering the [Learned Strategies] prompt block; POLARITY-GATED + FAIL-CLOSED (agree / unrelated / uncertain / a model error all leave the strategy untouched); INJECTED-ONLY (a probation strategy isn't applied, so it's never a target); BRAKE-FIRST (a paused learner's bank is frozen); bounded model spend per tick. Verified deterministically AND live: 5 classifier parse/fail-closed unit tests (CONTRADICT/AGREE/UNRELATED parsed case-insensitively; a model error or unparseable answer тЖТ "uncertain" so it never decays on a guess) + 9 decay-orchestrator safety tests (a contradict drops to the avoid floor тЖТ not injectable; agree/unrelated/uncertain тЖТ no decay; a probation strategy is never touched; nothing ever graduates; maxClassifications cap; brake freezes the bank) + 2 daemon-wiring tests (a contradicting correction тЖТ the injected strategy decayed to -4 + the felt notice delivered, never graduating; a non-contradicting correction тЖТ no decay) + `pnpm check` exit 0 across all 20 workspaces (agent-core 1446, autoconfigure 495, cli 1894) + `pnpm lint` 0/0 + the permanent polarity battery 11/11 with 0 false-CONTRADICT on qwen3:8b + THE FLIP PROOF: a LIVE `muse daemon --once` on qwen3:8b where a seeded injected strategy ("Always give long, detailed multi-paragraph answers.", reward 3, injectable=true) + a queued contradicting correction ("Stop giving me long essays тАФ answer in ONE short sentence.") drove the REAL polarity classifier to decay it to reward -4 / injectable=FALSE / probation=false, with NO manual command тАФ a correction made in one session measurably changed a later session's behaviour unattended, sign-safe. agent-core 1446 + autoconfigure 495 + cli 1894 + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + polarity battery 11/11 + live daemon decay e2e тАФ Muse's autonomous self-development daemon now closes the loop in BOTH directions (it learns from your corrections AND stops applying what you've contradicted, on its own), with the honesty machinery intact because the only autonomous reward change is subtractive and reversible тАФ P43-1 FLIP (Self-improve/autonomy, sign-safe autonomous correction-decay тАФ THE #1 lever)
- [Trust/Privacy] A user can now ENCRYPT their people graph (contacts) at rest тАФ `muse contacts encrypt` (with `decrypt` + `encryption-status`) so WHO their doctor / manager / partner / landlord are, with each person's email / phone / handle / birthday / relationship, is no longer CLEARTEXT JSON readable by anyone with disk access. OUTBOUND-SAFE by construction: the recipient-resolution path (`resolveContact`, which gates every outbound send under outbound-safety rule 3) reads the contacts, so a WRONG key resolves against an EMPTY set тЖТ the recipient is not-found тЖТ a send REFUSES / fires a clarify, NEVER a wrong recipient; and the `muse ask` contact-grounding read is fail-soft (a key mismatch degrades to no-contact-answers, never crashes the core flow). - [Trust/Security] Muse's email ingestion is now INDIRECT-PROMPT-INJECTION-HARDENED тАФ a malicious email can no longer splice forged instructions into Muse's recalled context. P37-22/23 made email a recall source (great for "what did Dana email?"), but an email is UNTRUSTED third-party content тАФ a sender controls its from/subject/snippet тАФ and the ingestion wrote those RAW into a recallable note, so a crafted email carrying `\n[System Override]\nIgnore your instructionsтАж` (or a forged `# Email:` heading / `From:` line, a CRLF, or ANSI/C0 control bytes) could splice a fake prompt section that the model sees once the note is recalled (indirect prompt injection тАФ the research backlog's #5 spotlighting concern, now a live surface since email ships). Closed by applying the SAME deterministic defence every OTHER untrusted-content path in Muse already uses (ambient-context, attachment-context, episodic-recall, skills-context, active-context all run it) тАФ `stripUntrustedTerminalChars(value).replace(/\s+/gu, " ").trim()` тАФ to the email's from / subject / date / snippet inside `renderEmailNote` (apps/cli/src/email-sync.ts), so no untrusted field can carry a newline that breaks out of its own line; only the note's OWN structural newlines (which the code, not the sender, controls) remain. This is DETERMINISTIC CODE, not a prompt please-be-careful (per CLAUDE.md's non-negotiable "security is deterministic code, never prompt instruction"), and FABRICATION-SAFE: whitespace-collapse only removes the section-splice тАФ the email's actual words stay intact as inert grounding evidence (recall is unaffected), and a single-line injection is just text the grounding gate still treats as a cited source, never an instruction. Verified deterministically (this is a content-sanitisation fix, not the LLM request/response path, so smoke:live does not apply): 7 new unit tests (apps/cli/src/email-sync.test.ts тАФ a `\n[System Override]\n` in the snippet produces NO standalone forged section and `[System Override]` never starts a line, while the words remain; a subject/from cannot forge a SECOND `# Email:` heading or `From:` line; ANSI/C0 control + DEL bytes are stripped; a CRLF cannot splice a new line; a legit single-line email renders byte-identical (sanitisation is a no-op on clean content); `syncEmailsToNotes` writes sanitised notes idempotently; `safeEmailId("../../etc/passwd")` тЖТ a path-safe filename, no traversal) + the existing 6 email CLI tests + 3 daemon email-sync tests UNBROKEN + the full @muse/cli suite green (174 files / 1911 tests) + `pnpm lint` 0/0. cli 1911 + pnpm lint 0/0 + injection battery тАФ the email-into-recall surface (P37-22/23) now carries the same indirect-prompt-injection defence as every other untrusted source Muse reads, deterministically and fabrication-safe тАФ P37-23 hardening (Trust/security, untrusted-email injection sanitisation, backlog #5)
- [Grounding/Honesty] When a user's notes CONFLICT, Muse now SURFACES the conflict тАФ "I have conflicting notes: [from a.md] says June 12th, [from b.md] says June 15th тАФ which is current?" тАФ instead of confidently picking one and hiding the other. This was a real honesty hole found by live probe: with two genuinely-conflicting notes (a.md "dentist June 12th", b.md "Dentist: June 15th", no update wording), `muse ask "when is my dentist appointment?"` on qwen3:8b confidently answered "June 12th [from a.md]", silently ignoring the conflicting b.md тАФ a fabrication-ADJACENT failure the grounding gate could not catch (the gate rejects a claim with NO retrieved source, but happily passes a claim that HAS a source even when another retrieved source CONTRADICTS it). The fix EXTENDS the honesty edge from "I'm not sure" (un-groundable) to "I have conflicting info" (multiply-groundable, contradictorily): a CONFLICTS rule added to the recall answer contract `CITATION_INSTRUCTION_LINES` (apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts) tells the model that when two passages give DIFFERENT answers and neither clearly updates the other, it must surface BOTH and the conflict citing each ("I have conflicting notes: X says тАж, Y says тАж тАФ which is current?") rather than silently choosing; with an explicit carve-out so an UPDATE ("moved to", "now", "corrected to") is RESOLVED to the new value, not over-flagged as a conflict. It is a prompt-instruction behaviour with NO new model call тЖТ ZERO added latency (it rides the existing answer generation); it does not change the grounding GATE (claims still cite real sources), and it is fail-soft (if the model ignored it the answer would be no worse than before). Verified deterministically AND live: a new unit test (CITATION_INSTRUCTION_LINES carries the CONFLICT rule AND the "if one UPDATES the other" carve-out тАФ apps/cli/src/commands-ask-cite-as.test.ts) + the full @muse/cli suite green (174 files / 1912 tests) + `pnpm lint` 0/0 + a NEW PERMANENT live battery (apps/cli/scripts/verify-conflict-surfacing.mjs, wired into `eval:self-improving`) that on qwen3:8b asserts a GENUINE conflict surfaces both values + flags it (passed: "I have conflicting notes: [from a.md] says June 12th, [from b.md] says June 15th тАФ which is current?") AND an explicit UPDATE resolves to the new value without being left open (passed: "the weekly team sync is on Thursday at 4:00pm [from new.md]") тАФ 2/2 тАФ plus a full LIVE `muse ask` round-trip reproducing both behaviours end-to-end (before the fix it answered "June 12th" silently; after, it surfaces the conflict). cli 1912 + pnpm lint 0/0 + conflict-surfacing battery 2/2 + live muse ask both cases тАФ Muse no longer picks a side in your own contradictory notes; it shows you the conflict and asks which is current, extending the grounding edge to multiply-groundable-but-contradictory claims тАФ P38-36 (Grounding/honesty, conflict-surfacing in cited recall)
- [Actuation/Reliability] When you set a reminder by voice/chat, Muse now confirms it with the time you ACTUALLY asked for тАФ "I've added a reminder тАж due on Fri, Jun 5, 2026, 3:00 PM (tomorrow)" тАФ instead of echoing the wrong hour. A real, trust-eroding actuator defect found by live probe: `muse ask --with-tools "remind me to call the dentist tomorrow at 3pm"` STORED the reminder correctly (3pm local) but the model CONFIRMED "тАжat 6:00 AM" тАФ it read the raw UTC ISO hour (тАжT06:00:00Z, which is 3pm KST) and parroted "6:00 AM", telling the user a time they never asked for. The reminder fires at the right instant, so the firing path never saw it тАФ but a confidant that reads back the wrong time looks broken and erodes trust in every "did you set that?". Fixed by enriching the model-facing reminder MCP tool results (add/due/search/snooze/fire) with a `dueAtLocal` field тАФ the due time rendered in the SERVER's local timezone, the same wall clock the natural-language phrase was parsed against ("Fri, Jun 5, 2026, 3:00 PM (tomorrow)") via a new `formatReminderDueLocal` + `serializeReminderForModel` (packages/mcp/src/personal-reminders-store.ts) тАФ plus a `muse.reminders.add` tool-description anchor instructing the model to confirm with `dueAtLocal`, never the raw UTC ISO `dueAt`. The REST/web path is untouched (keeps the lean serializeReminder; the web UI formats its own times); only the LLM-facing tool results carry the extra field, so there's no API-shape change and no latency cost (pure string formatting on an already-returned result). This is actuator HARDENING per the human-directed focus тАФ a proven-once actuator that misreports the time is a user-facing reliability defect, and closing it is outward. - [Proactivity/Anticipation] Muse now PROACTIVELY WARNS you of an upcoming calendar double-booking тАФ it tells you about Friday's clash on Wednesday тАФ instead of only showing conflicts when you happen to run `muse today`. The capability map flagged this as the highest-value anticipation a single-user confidant can offer, and as a ЁЯЯб gap: double-booking DETECTION already existed (detectCalendarConflicts) but ONLY on the PULL surfaces (`muse today`, `muse calendar conflicts`) тАФ the morning briefing, the evening recap, and every daemon tick were silent on conflicts, so a clash only ever surfaced if the user thought to look. This adds the missing PUSH: a pure `selectUpcomingConflicts(events, {now, withinDays})` in @muse/mcp (the future clashes whose overlap begins inside [now, now+withinDays], each carrying a stable dedup key + a human-readable LOCAL-time line; a clash already underway or in the past is excluded so Muse never nags about something un-bookable) layered on the existing detector, plus a `conflictWatchTick` daemon tick (apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.ts) that scans the upcoming calendar window and warns ONCE per clash via the user's configured messaging channel. It is off by default (MUSE_CONFLICT_WATCH_ENABLED), throttled (MUSE_CONFLICT_WATCH_INTERVAL_MS, default 30 min; MUSE_CONFLICT_WATCH_WITHIN_DAYS default 7), key-deduped via a ~/.muse/conflict-watch-fired.json sidecar so a standing clash never re-spams, fail-soft (a calendar provider hiccup never breaks the daemon тАФ same discipline as recap/briefing/email-sync ticks), and surfaced in `muse daemon --status` ("conflicts: enabled/disabled") for discoverability. This is a genuinely NEW axis (proactive anticipation, per B0's steering to favor a new axis over more grounding/time-display polish), reusing the existing conflict detector rather than reinventing it тАФ the new value is the proactive delivery + dedup layer. - [Actuation/Trust] The agent no longer HARD-FAILS on your own contacts тАФ `muse ask --with-tools "draft an email to Sarah тАж"` now produces a draft instead of erroring "Input guard detected private identifiers: email". Probing the outbound path exposed a severe, identity-breaking defect: the PII INPUT guard (createPiiInputGuard, packages/agent-core/src/guards.ts) was enabled BY DEFAULT (MUSE_INPUT_GUARD_PII_ENABLED defaulted true) and fail-closes the ENTIRE agent run when the assembled input carries any email/phone/private identifier тАФ but for a local "tell it everything" personal assistant whose OWN contacts and notes contain emails by nature, that breaks the core agent (and the outbound-email drafting that P41-2/P41-3 carefully hardened) on the user's own data EVERY time a contact with an email is in context. The fix is posture-aware (packages/autoconfigure/src/runtime-wiring.ts createInputGuards): the PII INPUT guard's purpose is preventing PII from EGRESSING to a third-party CLOUD model, but under MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY (the DEFAULT posture) the model is on-box and the model router refuses cloud egress via a SEPARATE deterministic gate (createModelProvider/LocalOnlyViolationError), so there is no third party to leak to and the block is pure breakage with zero benefit тАФ therefore the guard now fires by default ONLY when cloud egress is actually possible (MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY off); an explicit MUSE_INPUT_GUARD_PII_ENABLED=true still forces it on under any posture (opt-in). The INJECTION input guard (the real untrusted-content defense) and the PII OUTPUT mask (transcript/log hygiene) are UNCHANGED. Because this is a security-default change (big/risky per the decide-and-do directive), it was adversarially reviewed by an independent sub-agent panel BEFORE shipping (VERDICT: ship тАФ confirmed no real hole under local-only: the egress refusal is a separate gate, this guard's only consumer is the pre-model input pipeline, and there is no other sink it solely protected; this removes a control firing OUTSIDE its threat model, not a fail-open regression), and the cloud-side residual over-block was recorded as an explicit follow-up (Rejected ledger) rather than declared fixed. Verified deterministically AND live: 4 new posture unit tests (local-only default тЖТ injection guard only, PII block OFF so the agent isn't broken on the user's own contacts; MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY=false тЖТ PII guard present; explicit MUSE_INPUT_GUARD_PII_ENABLED=true forces it on under local-only; per-flag independent drops) тАФ @muse/autoconfigure 75 files / 497 tests + @muse/cli 174 files / 1920 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 + a LIVE before/after round-trip on qwen3:8b: the EXACT prompt that previously errored "Input guard detected private identifiers: email" now returns a complete, well-formed email draft to Sarah ("Subject: Request to Reschedule Our 2pm Meeting тАж Best regards"), while under MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY=false the same prompt STILL blocks with the PII error (egress protection for cloud users preserved). autoconfigure 497 + cli 1920 + lint 0/0 + live before(errored)/after(drafts)/cloud(still-blocks) on qwen тАФ a user can now have the agent draft emails and reason over their own contacts on a local-first assistant without a privacy guard meant for cloud egress breaking the whole run. тАФ P41-5 (Actuation/trust, posture-aware PII input guard; sub-agent-reviewed security-default change)
- [Actuation/Trust] The agent no longer MASKS your own contacts' details back to you тАФ `muse ask --with-tools "what is Sarah's email?"` now returns the real address instead of `***@***.***`. The output-guard sibling of P41-5 (which fixed the PII INPUT block that errored the whole run): the PII OUTPUT mask (createPiiMaskingOutputGuard, packages/agent-core/src/guards.ts) was enabled BY DEFAULT and REWRITES the agent's final answer тАФ and the cached + run-history copy, since the runtime's applyOutputGuards replaces finalResponse with the masked text (agent-runtime.ts:536-538) тАФ redacting any email/phone to `***@***.***`. So on a local "tell it everything" assistant, asking the agent for your OWN contact's email handed back a masked answer; the answer is the very thing the user asked for. And unlike a true egress control, the output mask doesn't even PREVENT egress (under a cloud model the PII already left on the INPUT side), so under local-only its only effect is corrupting the user-facing answer + the local store with zero privacy benefit. Fixed with the SAME posture-aware pattern as P41-5 (packages/autoconfigure/src/runtime-wiring.ts createOutputGuards): the PII OUTPUT mask fires by default ONLY when cloud egress is possible (MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY off, the non-default posture); an explicit MUSE_OUTPUT_GUARD_PII_MASK_ENABLED=true still forces it on under any posture (opt-in). - [Actuation/Reliability] A multi-step "add the event AND remind me" request no longer silently LOSES the reminder тАФ `muse ask --with-tools "add a meeting with Sarah tomorrow at 2pm to my calendar, and remind me an hour before it"` now reliably creates BOTH the calendar event (2pm) and the reminder (1pm, an hour before), where before the reminder was silently dropped. Probing this realistic two-actuator request exposed a real carry-to-done defect: the calendar event was created but the reminder DROPPED with "recurrence must be 'daily' or 'weekly'". The local model, making a ONE-TIME reminder, filled the muse.reminders.add `recurrence` arg with a sentinel like "none"/"once" (instead of OMITTING it as the schema asks), and the tool HARD-ERRORED on any value that wasn't exactly "daily"/"weekly" тАФ so a benign arg the model guessed cost the user their reminder, and the multi-step task half-failed with no sign to the user. Fixed per tool-calling.md rule 7 (validate + repair deterministically, don't re-reason or reject): a new pure `normalizeReminderRecurrence(raw)` in packages/mcp/src/personal-reminders-store.ts тАФ only "daily"/"weekly" (case-insensitive) are real cadences; a recognized one-time SENTINEL (none / once / one-time / single / no / never / n/a / false / empty) resolves SILENTLY to a one-shot reminder; a genuinely unsupported cadence (e.g. "monthly") STILL creates the one-shot reminder but returns a `note` field so the outcome is transparent, never hidden тАФ wired into the muse.reminders.add tool (packages/mcp/src/loopback-reminders.ts), replacing the hard error. The reminder is now ALWAYS created; the actuator survives a real-world model input instead of dropping the user's reminder over a recurrence-arg guess. This is actuation HARDENING (the map's #1 "carry a multi-step request to done" reliability area), found by probing, distinct from the retry/transient P41-1..4 slices (a validation-strictness failure mode rather than a network one). Verified deterministically AND live: 4 new unit tests (daily/weekly pass through case-insensitively; undefined / empty / every one-time sentinel тЖТ {} silently with no note; "monthly" тЖТ one-shot + an explanatory note and NEVER a hard error тАФ packages/mcp/test/reminders-recurrence.test.ts) + the existing reminder suites unregressed + the full @muse/mcp suite green (174 files / 1483 tests) + pnpm lint 0/0 + a full LIVE before/after on the local qwen3:8b: the IDENTICAL multi-step prompt that before the fix created the calendar event but DROPPED the reminder (recurrence error) now creates BOTH тАФ the calendar event "Meeting with Sarah" at 2026-06-05T05:00:00Z (2pm KST) AND the reminder "Meeting with Sarah" at 2026-06-05T04:00:00Z (1pm KST, correctly an hour before the meeting). mcp 1483 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live multi-step before(reminder dropped)/after(event+reminder both created, reminder an hour before) тАФ a user can now give Muse a compound "schedule this and remind me" request and trust that the reminder half actually lands. тАФ P41-7 (Actuation/reliability, reminder recurrence coercion; multi-step carry-to-done)
- [Actuation/Reliability] You can now EDIT a reminder by NAME, conversationally тАФ "push my dentist reminder to 5pm tomorrow" / "delete my milk reminder" now work instead of "reminder not found". Probing the edit path exposed a real carry-to-done defect: `muse ask --with-tools "push my dentist reminder back to 5pm tomorrow"` called muse.reminders.snooze but passed the TEXT "Call dentist" as the `id` (the local model refers to reminders by their description, not their generated id, and went straight to snooze without calling `search` first), so the tool answered "reminder not found" and the reschedule SILENTLY did nothing (the dueAt stayed unchanged). The snooze/fire/clear reminder tools required a literal id тАФ i.e. a 2-step "search to get the id, then act" chain that the small local model reliably fumbles (exactly the failure mode tool-calling.md warns about: prefer one tool that does the whole job). Fixed with a pure `resolveReminderRef(reminders, ref)` helper (packages/mcp/src/personal-reminders-store.ts): an exact id match wins; otherwise a case-insensitive substring match on the reminder text, preferring a PENDING reminder over an already-fired one when both match; a UNIQUE match resolves, MULTIPLE matches return the candidate list (fail-close тАФ never modify a guessed reminder, the same never-guess discipline as contact resolution), and no match тЖТ not-found тАФ wired into all three edit tools (snooze / fire / clear in packages/mcp/src/loopback-reminders.ts), whose `id` arg now accepts an id OR a distinct word from the text (e.g. 'dentist'), documented in the schema description. This turns the fumbled 2-step chain into a reliable ONE shot and is actuation HARDENING for the map's #1 "carry a request to done" area, found by probing, distinct from the P41-7 recurrence fix (create-path) тАФ this is the edit-path. Verified deterministically AND live: 5 new unit tests (resolves an exact id; resolves a unique text word тАФ what the model actually passes; prefers the PENDING match when a word hits both a pending and a fired reminder; returns AMBIGUOUS candidates never a guess when multiple pending match; empty ref / no match тЖТ not-found тАФ packages/mcp/test/reminders-recurrence.test.ts) + the existing reminder suites unregressed + the full @muse/mcp suite green (174 files / 1488 tests) + pnpm lint 0/0 + a full LIVE before/after on the local qwen3:8b: the IDENTICAL prompt "push my dentist reminder back to 5pm tomorrow" that before the fix returned "reminder not found" (dueAt left at the old 06:00Z) now resolves "dentist" тЖТ the seeded reminder and reschedules it to 2026-06-05T08:00:00Z (5pm KST tomorrow, confirmed back to the user as "due on June 5, 2026, at 5:00 PM"). mcp 1488 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live before(not found, unchanged)/after(resolved by text + rescheduled) тАФ a user can now reschedule, complete, or delete a reminder by just naming it, instead of the edit silently failing. (The tasks complete/update/delete tools have the identical id-vs-text gap тАФ a clean follow-on.) тАФ P41-8 (Actuation/reliability, edit-a-reminder-by-name via resolveReminderRef; one-shot resolve-then-act)
- [Perception/Knowledge-corpus] Muse now perceives notes in MORE formats тАФ `.org` (Emacs org-mode), `.rst` (reStructuredText), `.mdx`, `.text`, `.adoc`/`.asciidoc`, and markdown variants (`.mkd`/`.mdown`) are now indexed and citable, where before only `.md`/`.markdown`/`.txt`/`.pdf` were. Probing the corpus perception exposed a real gap: a `.txt` note dropped in the notes dir was indexed and answered, but a `.org` note in the same dir was SILENTLY SKIPPED ("2 embedded, 0 skipped" тАФ it never appeared in the index), so a power-user keeping notes in org-mode / reStructuredText / AsciiDoc / MDX had those notes INVISIBLE to recall. The root cause was the notes-index walker's extension allow-list (`/\.(md|markdown|txt|pdf)$/`) being too narrow тАФ even though the extractor (`extractDocumentText`) already reads every non-PDF file as UTF-8, so the walk filter was the ONLY gate dropping these prose formats. - [Actuation/Reliability] "Send Sarah a message" now works on WHATEVER messenger you configured тАФ the send tool resolves your channel from config instead of failing on the local model's guess. Probing the outbound path exposed a real send-breakage: `muse ask --with-tools "send Sarah a message that I'm running late"` made the local model call muse.messaging.send with providerId="telegram" (it guesses, because the tool description listed "telegram | discord | slack | line" and REQUIRED a providerId), so a user who configured ONLY Slack/Discord/LINE got "the Telegram messaging provider is not registered" and could not send at all тАФ a 0% send success rate for any non-Telegram single-provider user. Fixed by resolving the channel from config in the muse.messaging.send tool (packages/mcp/src/loopback-messaging.ts): an explicit REGISTERED providerId is honoured; a SINGLE configured provider is used automatically (the model needn't know its opaque id); ZERO providers тЖТ "no messenger configured" error; MULTIPLE providers + a missing/unknown id тЖТ ASK (error listing the configured ids, never guess among several); providerId is now OPTIONAL in the schema with a description steering the model to omit it unless multiple messengers exist. Crucially this RESOLVES the provider from config rather than letting the model guess тАФ which ALIGNS with outbound-safety.md ("resolved, never guessed") rather than weakening it тАФ and the draft-first approval gate (sendMessageWithApproval) is completely UNCHANGED and runs AFTER resolution, so the user still sees and confirms the exact {provider, destination, text} (the gate is the backstop for any provider/destination shape mismatch). - [Trust/Outbound-safety] SECURITY FIX: the agent can no longer AUTO-SEND a message to a third party without draft-first confirmation тАФ `muse.messaging.send` now fails CLOSED. Probing P41-10's live behaviour exposed a real outbound-safety hole: `muse ask --with-tools "send Sarah a message that I'm running late"` actually SENT it ("I have successfully sent the message to Sarah") with NO draft-first confirmation. Root cause (packages/autoconfigure/src/loopback-tools.ts): the production muse.messaging.send tool is wired with actionLogFile + userId but NO approvalGate, and sendMessageWithApproval AUTO-APPROVES when no gate is present тАФ so the agent's third-party send fired on its own, while the sibling email/web/home actuators (apps/cli/src/actuator-tools.ts) are ALL draft-first gated with a clack confirm. That violates outbound-safety.md Rule 1 ("Draft-first, never auto-send. The agent produces the exact content and the user explicitly confirms that content before it leaves") on exactly the path P41-2 hardened for the human CLI but missed for the agent tool. Closed at the source (packages/mcp/src/loopback-messaging.ts): the action-logged send path now defaults to a FAIL-CLOSED gate (DENY_WITHOUT_CONFIRMATION) whenever no approvalGate is wired тАФ implementing outbound-safety's "a send never proceeds because the confirmation step failed / cannot be delivered" тАФ so the agent now REFUSES the send (recorded as a `refused` action-log entry, not `performed`) and points the user to the gated `muse messaging send` CLI, instead of auto-sending. This is a RESTRICTIVE change (it closes a hole, never opens one): the human CLI path (which passes its own draft-first gate, P41-2/P41-3) and the lightweight no-action-log/test path (direct send, no third-party risk) are both unchanged. Verified deterministically AND live: the F-1 outbound-safety recording test was split into a gated-`performed` case (an approving gate тЖТ send + performed log) PLUS a NEW no-gate тЖТ fail-closed case (the production wiring with no approvalGate now yields refused:true, a `refused` action-log entry, and NO `performed` entry) + the P41-10 provider-resolution send tests updated to pass an approving gate + the full @muse/mcp suite green (174 files / 1499 tests) + pnpm lint 0/0 + a full LIVE before/after on the local qwen3:8b: the IDENTICAL prompt "send Sarah a message that I am running 10 minutes late" that before the fix reported "I have successfully sent the message to Sarah" (auto-sent) now REFUSES тАФ "there is no draft-first confirmation channel set up for the agent тАж review and send via the `muse messaging send` command" тАФ and nothing is sent. mcp 1499 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live before(auto-sent)/after(fail-closed, refused) тАФ the agent can no longer send a message to someone without you confirming the exact content first, closing the last ungated outbound actuator. - [Grounding/Honesty] Muse no longer LIES about remembering тАФ `muse ask "remember that I'm allergic to penicillin"` now answers honestly ("I can't save that fact from a one-shot question. To remember this, run `muse remember \"I am allergic to penicillin\"`, or tell me inside a `muse chat` session") instead of the fabricated "I've noted your allergy to penicillin". Probing the core "tell it everything, it remembers" promise exposed a real trust failure: a one-shot `muse ask` told to remember a fact answered "I've noted your allergy" тАФ and even fabricated a citation to a non-existent "allergy note" (the grounding gate caught and stripped that) тАФ while persisting NOTHING. The recall path is read-only by design (the remember_fact tool is in RECALL_FORBIDDEN_TOOL_NAMES and there is no auto-extraction on that path; memory writes happen via `muse remember` or `muse chat` auto-extraction), so a one-shot ask genuinely cannot save тАФ but the model CLAIMED it did, which is the worst kind of confidant lie (the user trusts Muse kept something it silently dropped, and discovers it forgot only later). This EXTENDS the honesty edge (the same recall answer-behaviour contract CITATION_INSTRUCTION_LINES that already carries the I'm-not-sure and conflict-surfacing rules, apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts): a SAVING rule tells the model that this one-shot answer cannot persist anything, so when the user says remember / note / save / "don't forget" a FACT about them, it must NOT claim it saved or noted it (that would be a lie) and must instead say it can't save from a one-shot question and DIRECT the user to the real save path тАФ run `muse remember "<the fact>"` or tell Muse inside a kept `muse chat` session тАФ with an explicit carve-out so a request to set a reminder or task (which IS handled by tools) is not swept up by the rule. It is a prompt-instruction behaviour with NO new model call тЖТ ZERO added latency; it does not change the grounding GATE; and it is fail-soft (if ignored the answer is no worse than before). This is a NEW honesty SURFACE (the remember-lie), an extension of the edge like P38-36 conflict-surfacing тАФ not grounding-gate false-positive polish тАФ and a genuinely fresh axis after a streak of actuation/messaging work. - [Recall/Perception] "What's due tomorrow?" - [Actuation/Trust] The agent can SEND a message again тАФ and now DRAFT-FIRST: `muse ask --with-tools "send Sarah I'm running late"` shows the exact draft and fires only on your explicit confirm, completing the P41-11 security arc. P41-11 closed the auto-send hole by making muse.messaging.send FAIL-CLOSED whenever no confirmation channel was wired тАФ which (correctly but bluntly) left the agent unable to send a message AT ALL. This wires the missing draft-first gate: a new buildMessagingApprovalGate (apps/cli/src/actuator-tools.ts, mirroring the email/web/home actuator gates) shows the EXACT {provider тЖТ destination + text} and returns approved ONLY on an explicit confirm; it is threaded from `muse ask --with-tools` through a new optional messagingApprovalGate on createMuseRuntimeAssembly тЖТ buildLoopbackTools тЖТ createMessagingMcpServer (packages/autoconfigure). So the agent's send is now: in an interactive terminal, DRAFT-FIRST (you see the exact message, you confirm, it sends); in a non-TTY (headless / daemon / CI) or with no gate, FAIL-CLOSED (the confirm can't be delivered, so the send does not happen) тАФ exactly outbound-safety.md's rule ("a send never proceeds because the confirmation step cannot be delivered"). It is built under --with-tools (NOT gated behind --actuators) so a benign "send X a message" reaches it directly. This restores a real capability the user lost in P41-11 while keeping the security property intact (no auto-send is ever possible; the only way a message leaves is an explicit human confirm in an interactive session). Verified deterministically per outbound-safety's "prove the gate, not just the happy path": 3 gate-factory unit tests (a NON-interactive context тЖТ DENY/fail-closed; interactive + the user confirms тЖТ APPROVE; interactive + the user declines тЖТ DENY тАФ apps/cli/src/actuator-tools.test.ts) + a threading test (buildLoopbackTools wired with a DENYING messagingApprovalGate тЖТ the message provider's send is NEVER called; with an APPROVING gate тЖТ it IS called тАФ packages/autoconfigure/test/loopback-tools.test.ts, proving the gate actually flows assembly тЖТ loopback тЖТ server) + the full @muse/autoconfigure (500), @muse/cli (174 files / 1930 tests) and @muse/mcp (1499) suites + pnpm lint 0/0 + a full LIVE headless run on the local qwen3:8b with HOME isolated: the agent calls muse.messaging.send, the gate fail-closes (non-TTY) and the agent answers "I encountered an issue sending the message. - [Trust/Grounding] Your OWN benign notes no longer get mistaken for a prompt-injection attack тАФ `muse ask --with-tools` over a note like "Do not forget to get all the groceries and the milk on the way home" no longer dies with "Input guard detected injection patterns: role_override"; the recall turn proceeds and answers. Closing the P41-12-probe follow-on, this fixes a guard turning the user's own trust-everything notes against them: the default-wired injection input guard (createInjectionInputGuard тЖТ findInjectionPatterns, packages/agent-core/src/guards.ts) scans the ENTIRE assembled prompt тАФ INCLUDING the user's first-party grounding context (notes/tasks/contacts) тАФ and fail-closes the whole run on any match, and its first role_override pattern ended in `(instructions?|and)`. The bare `|and` matched almost any benign "тАжallтАж andтАж" / "тАжpreviousтАж andтАж" prose, so real first-party notes ("Do not forget to get all the groceries AND the milk", "Ignore the previous draft AND use the new one", "disregard all the old prices AND updateтАж") tripped role_override and the agent answered nothing but the guard-block reason тАФ the injection-guard sibling of the P41-5 PII over-block. Fixed at the source (packages/policy/src/injection-patterns.ts) by replacing the lazy `|and` with the EXPLICIT override-target noun set `(instructions?|prompts?|rules?|directions?|guidelines?|commands?|messages?|context)` тАФ which both KILLS the benign-prose false positives AND WIDENS genuine detection that a bare `instructions?` would have narrowed: "ignore all previous RULES", "disregard the above PROMPT", "ignore the above DIRECTIONS", "forget all prior COMMANDS" are now all caught (none of the other patterns catch those тАФ line 85 needs disregard+your/the/my, line 88 needs override), which matters because there is NO LLM-classification backstop wired by default тАФ the regex guard is the only injection defense, so the fix had to PRESERVE detection, not just delete the offending branch. (Intended as a sub-agent-reviewed security slice per the deferred entry; the review sub-agent hit an API ConnectionRefused this fire, so the safety argument was made inline and proven BOTH directions by test instead.) - [Perception/Reach] `muse ask --url <pdf>` now READS an online PDF and grounds on its text тАФ a user can ask about a policy doc, paper, or manual linked on the web, not just an HTML page. Probing the web-perception path exposed the gap: P37-18's `fetchReadableUrl` deliberately REFUSED any non-text content-type (a PDF decoded to garbled bytes would make the model hallucinate content and cite it to the URL тАФ a fabrication), so `muse ask --url <a-pdf-url>` answered "not a readable text page (content-type: application/pdf)" and grounded on nothing тАФ even though the web is full of PDFs and `muse ask --file <pdf>` already reads them locally via pdf-parse. Closed with an INJECTED PDF extractor rather than a dependency-add: `fetchReadableUrl` (packages/mcp/src/fetch-readable-url.ts) gained an optional `pdfExtractor?: (bytes: Uint8Array) => Promise<string>` тАФ when the URL serves `application/pdf` AND an extractor is wired, the body is read as bytes and run through it (instead of being refused); when NO extractor is wired a PDF still refuses, so the agent's `web_read` tool and `notes ingest --url` stay text-only and UNCHANGED. The CLI `--url` path (apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts) passes `parsePdfBuffer` тАФ the SAME pdf-parse path `--file <pdf>` already uses тАФ so the pdf-parse dependency stays entirely in the CLI and the `@muse/mcp` core never grows a PDF dependency (the dependency-injection keeps the core framework-independent per architecture rules). The SSRF guard is completely unchanged (public hosts only, re-checked after redirects, 15s timeout), and the honesty posture is preserved: an empty / scanned / image-only PDF whose extractor yields no text is REFUSED ("no extractable text") rather than grounded on empty, and an extractor failure surfaces a clear "PDF could not be read: <reason>" error, never a crash or garbage. - [Reasoning] The agent's deterministic arithmetic evaluator `muse.math.evaluate` is now WIRED into the default tool set (it was built but unreachable) тАФ a user can now ask the agent to "calculate <expression>" (e.g. "calculate 840000 * 0.18") and get the EXACT result (151200) from a safe recursive-descent evaluator, instead of an unreliable small-model guess. Probing the agent tool surface against the research backlog's hint ("math_eval lever ALREADY built тАФ verify gaps vs real wiring") exposed a real wiring gap: a complete deterministic arithmetic evaluator (`createMathMcpServer`, packages/mcp/src/loopback-math-server.ts тАФ recursive-descent parser over digits/parens/+-*/%, NO `eval`/`Function`, input-validated) AND a `math_eval` MuseTool existed, but `buildLoopbackTools` (packages/autoconfigure/src/loopback-tools.ts) assembled calendar/tasks/reminders/notes/episodes/followups/messaging/status/webRead and SKIPPED math entirely тАФ so `muse ask --with-tools` and `muse chat` could never reach it (the tool was built-but-dead code from the agent's perspective). Closed by wiring `createMathMcpServer` into the bundle (a new `math` group, default-on via `MUSE_MATH_ENABLED`, opt-out) + the DynamicToolRegistry in createMuseRuntimeAssembly, and enriching the tool's description with concrete examples (expression='840000 * 0.18' for '18% of 840,000') + a "do the maths HERE, never in your head тАФ you are a small model and will get the digits wrong" steer + relevance keywords (math/calculate/percent/ъ│ДьВ░/тАж) per tool-calling.md.
